# Changes vs upstream Calibre-Web-Automated

Tracks every divergence between this fork and `crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated@main` since the fork point. Updated per release.

Format: each row is one fork-PR, mapped to its upstream PR or issue (if any), with a one-line description and the squash-merge SHA.

| #135 | [#1346](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1346) | @navels | Avoid cover-thumbnail DB deadlock during metadata edits. `do_edit_book` previously called `helper.replace_cover_thumbnail_cache(book.id)` *inside* the Calibre metadata-edit transaction; the worker then re-opened `metadata.db` while the editing transaction was still holding a write lock, blocking the gevent loop and surfacing as 504s / 502s in the Web UI under any sustained ingest load. Fix defers the thumbnail queue until after `calibre_db.session.commit()` returns, and passes the committed `book.path` + `last_modified` directly into `TaskGenerateCoverThumbnails` via a new `BookCoverSource` dataclass so the worker no longer needs to re-query `metadata.db` for the single-book refresh case. Refs long-standing CWA [#1256](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1256) (4 reactions, 6 comments). Closes fork issue [#134](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/134) (reporter @Onkeyuk). 3 regression tests pin the post-commit ordering and the snapshot-passed code path. | `34f1985f` | v4.0.46 |
| #168 | [#1295](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1295) | @jgoguen | Mobile-Safari CSRF token for metadata search. iOS Safari does not reliably attach the `X-CSRFToken` header to `fetch()` requests, so `POST /metadata/search` was returning 400 / silently failing on iPhone — matches the user-visible complaint on CWA [#1266](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1266). Three layers: (1) `get_meta.js` now sends `csrf_token` in the request body for `/metadata/search` (body-borne CSRF is immune to Safari's header behavior); (2) new `cwaFetch()` helper in `layout.html` wraps `fetch()` and auto-attaches `X-CSRFToken` for any non-safe method (GET/HEAD/OPTIONS/TRACE bypass) when a token is present, without stomping on a caller-set header; (3) `main.js` ajaxSetup hardening — moves the `csrftoken` lookup from page-load cache into the per-request `beforeSend` handler with a null guard, so token rotation works and Safari's empty-string return path is handled. Existing CWA call sites in `cwa_convert_library.html` and `cwa_epub_fixer.html` routed through `cwaFetch()` for proactive coverage. Resolved one small conflict with our prior fork-original CSRF tweak by taking upstream's `.first().val()` pattern. 6 regression tests pin the cwaFetch helper, ajaxSetup hardening, body-CSRF inclusion, and call-site conversions. Closes fork issue [#154](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/154). Live verification on cwn-local with mobile-Safari user-agent: `POST /metadata/search` returns 200 with real provider results (Amazon, Apple Books, ComicVine). | `0026ac5a` | v4.0.54 |
| #169 | [#1271](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1271) | @jgoguen | KOReader plugin no-book guards. Tapping push or pull menu items when no book is open no longer crashes the plugin; new `showNoBookMessage()` and `ensureServerConfigured()` helpers wrap every push/pull entry point, and Pull-handler diagnostic logs are tightened to the `[Pull] end for <current_file> with <reason>` shape (richer than the older `body.<field> missing`). Landed alongside #1272 in the same fork PR. Server-side kosync routes verified unchanged via cwn-local probes (the patches are pure client-side). | #233 | [#1201](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1201) | @Sheol27 | **"Currently Reading" magic-shelf preset.** New `currently_reading` entry in `SYSTEM_SHELF_TEMPLATES` (read_status equal 2 = STATUS_IN_PROGRESS) so users can build a magic shelf that surfaces books KOSync/Kobo has marked in-progress. `yet_to_read` icon swapped 📖 → 📚 to avoid collision with the new preset. `build_filter_from_rule`'s no-custom-column branch refactored to handle all three statuses (STATUS_IN_PROGRESS / STATUS_FINISHED / STATUS_UNREAD) instead of treating read_status as boolean — in-progress books were previously silently falling through to "finished" matching. 7 regression tests in `tests/unit/test_magic_shelf_currently_reading.py` pin: preset existence + value 2, yet_to_read icon swap, source-pinned 3-status fallback. Diff: +50/-23 across `cps/magic_shelf.py` (+49/-22) and `cps/templates/magic_shelf_edit.html` (+1/-1). | `13b987ec` | v4.0.77 |
| #232 | [#1353](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1353) | @navels | **Incremental duplicate-key index — replaces the O(N) full-library duplicate scan with O(1) maintained-index lookups.** Stock CWA rebuilt duplicate groups from scratch on every scan (normalize title/author/series/publisher/format for every book in the library, then bucket into groups). With 10k+ book libraries this was slow and blocked other requests while it ran. **The fix**: new `cwa_duplicate_book_keys` SQL table (`book_id PK`, normalized title/author/language/series/publisher, format signature, criteria-aware fingerprint) maintained incrementally on every import, metadata edit, and deletion. New `cps/duplicate_index.py` (+578 LOC) exposes `upsert_book_keys`, `delete_book_keys`, `rebuild_duplicate_index`, `get_duplicate_groups_from_index`, `has_valid_duplicate_index_baseline`, `merge_affected_groups_into_cache`, `duplicate_index_needs_manual_full_scan`. Each book import (`add_book_to_library` / `add_format_to_book`) now calls `run_duplicate_scan_for_books([book_id])` inline via new `POST /cwa-internal/run-duplicate-scan` — single-book key upsert in milliseconds instead of full-library re-scan. Manual scans and ingest interlock via new `cwa_ingest_batch_active` marker file + `wait_for_duplicate_full_scan_to_finish()` in ingest_processor — ingest waits for any running full scan; manual full scans block during active ingest, exposed via new `POST /cwa-internal/duplicate-scan-status`. The Duplicates page renders a one-time-baseline-scan notice on fresh installs ("Duplicate scanning needs a one-time full scan. CWA now uses a duplicate index to keep duplicate checks fast during imports and metadata changes."); replaces alert dialogs with Bootstrap-modal feedback (Resolution Preview, success/error modals). **Reconciliation against fork-original work:** preserved PR #199 metadata.db flock (`metadata_db_write_lock()` + `_run_calibredb_add_with_retry`) — flock acquisition moved AFTER the new `mark_ingest_batch_active()` + `wait_for_duplicate_full_scan_to_finish()` calls in `add_book_to_library` so the active-marker check happens first, then the flock wraps the calibredb call as before. Preserved PR #210 debounce default 30 + clamp floor 10 across all 5 mirrored sites (rejected upstream's 60/5 — our PR #212 already eliminated the deadlock vector that motivated the conservative default; existing fork installs on 30 stay at 30, no new migration). Preserved PR #212 UDF connect-event listener (no `TaskReconnectDatabase` re-import; adopted `STAT_FINISH_SUCCESS, STAT_FAIL, STAT_ENDED, STAT_CANCELLED` to power new `_duplicate_full_scan_running()` worker-state check). Preserved PR #37/#56 `s6-setuidgid abc` privilege drop. Preserved v4.0.74/v4.0.75 fast-exit pattern (`_is_missing_ingest_target` + `_load_fork_cps_imports`). Preserved PR #100 batched cache-invalidation semantics — switched mechanism in `delete_selected_books` / `merge_list_book` from per-batch `invalidate_duplicate_cache()` to per-batch `_queue_duplicate_scan_after_change(book_ids)` (still one call per batch, just scoped to affected book IDs); `delete_book_from_table`'s skip-flag guard tightened to `if not skip_cache_invalidation and not refreshed_duplicate_cache` to avoid double-invalidate when the new indexed refresh handled it. Simplified `run_post_batch_follow_up()` to `/cwa-internal/reconnect-db` only — the deferred `invalidate-cache` + `queue-duplicate-scan` calls from #1349 are redundant in the new architecture (per-book incremental scans happen inline during ingest). **173 new + updated unit tests** across 6 test files (21 in `test_duplicate_index.py`, 4 in `test_duplicate_delete_index_maintenance.py`, 17 in `test_duplicate_scan_index_rewire.py`, 11 in `test_duplicate_scan_queue_settings.py`, 3 updated in `test_ingest_batch_dirty.py` for the active marker + wait-for-full-scan path, 3 updated PR #100 regression pins in `test_duplicate_manager_race_fix.py`). **Live container verification on cwn-local**: schema migration applied idempotently (`cwa_duplicate_book_keys` table + `idx_cwa_duplicate_book_keys_key` composite index created on first start; subsequent restarts are no-ops via CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS). Baseline scan populated index with 15 books — normalized title + composite duplicate_key + criteria fingerprint per row. /duplicates page identified existing groups ("Alice's Adventures in Wonderland" ×5, "The Republic" ×2) from the index in 22ms. Resolution Preview Bootstrap modal (replaces `alert()`) rendered KEEP/DELETE per-book breakdown with timestamps + formats in 0.02s for 2 groups using pre-scanned indexed groups. Sidebar "Duplicates: 2" badge updates from indexed cache. `POST /cwa-internal/run-duplicate-scan {"book_ids":[5,12,14,15,16]}` returned `{"message":"Duplicate scan completed: 1 new groups","result_count":1,"success":true}`. `POST /cwa-internal/duplicate-scan-status` returned `{"full_scan_running":false,"success":true}`. No console errors, no traceback. Inspired-by @navels in [#1353](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1353). | `3047debf` | v4.0.76 |
| #251 | [#1335](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1335) | @I-Would-Like-To-Report-A-Bug-Please | **Container reported healthy while ingest + metadata write-back silently broken; healthcheck curl had no bound; reverse-proxy keepalive sockets accumulated against wedged gevent process.** Three orthogonal failure-mode fixes shipped together because they all surface the same operator-facing symptom ("container says healthy, features don't work"). (1) **Dockerfile**: curl gains `--connect-timeout 1 --max-time 2` — a wedged gevent main loop (in-process worker holding the GIL through ingest / duplicate-scan / metadata edit) now produces a deterministic failed probe within 2s instead of relying on Docker's outer `--timeout=3s` to SIGTERM curl (signal propagation isn't always clean; recovery was unbounded). (2) **`cps/gevent_wsgi.py`**: new `read_request` override sets `self.close_connection = True` on every parsed request — stops stale reverse-proxy keepalive sockets accumulating against the gevent process, so recovery from a wedge is bounded. Verified behaviourally via `curl --next` reporting two distinct connection IDs for sequential requests. (3) **`cps/web.py`**: `/health` now probes critical s6 longruns (`cwa-ingest-service`, `metadata-change-detector`) via `s6-rc -a list` — the abc-readable primitive that `scripts/check-cwa-services.sh` already uses for the admin UI's "Check NextGen Status" action; `s6-svstat` won't work because supervise dirs are root-only in the lsio base image while the Flask app runs as `abc`. New `_CRITICAL_LONGRUNS` module-level tuple + `_check_s6_service_status` + `_probe_metadata_db` helpers; body gains a `services` map; any down longrun flips response to HTTP 503 with `status=degraded`. **Fork-original work bundled here**: the s6 service probe is fork-original (CWA #1335 only does the Dockerfile + gevent halves), addresses droM4X's explicit ask in #193 for service-liveness monitoring beyond DB consistency. 10 RED → GREEN regression tests across `test_health_service_status.py` (new, 7 tests), `test_dockerfile_healthcheck.py` (+2), `test_gevent_wsgi_format_request.py` (+1). **Live container verification on cwn-local**: baseline `{"services":{"cwa-ingest-service":"up","metadata-change-detector":"up"},"status":"ok"}` HTTP 200; `s6-rc -d change metadata-change-detector` → `{"services":{"...","metadata-change-detector":"down"},"status":"degraded"}` HTTP 503; restore → 200. 100 sequential probes all 200, 50 parallel max 0.10s, mid-stress toggle 30×503/30×200 deterministic, zero new ERROR/Traceback in logs. Reporters @droM4X (fork [#193](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/193)) and @FRaccie (~200k-book production trace). Backport credit @I-Would-Like-To-Report-A-Bug-Please. | `92c8cfa8` | v4.0.86 |
| #231 | [#1349](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1349) | @navels | **Stale-event filter + batch post-import follow-up + bounded internal-endpoint retries.** Five orthogonal ingest-reliability improvements. (1) `_is_missing_ingest_target()` fast-exits before runtime initialization or lock acquisition — eliminates the NFS/polling-fallback re-emit loop on already-moved files. (2) The s6 ingest-service script tracks per-file processing markers under `$PROCESSING_DIR` so the watcher can't reprocess a path while it's still being handled. (3) Module-import-time work (cps, CWA_DB, EPUBFixer, audiobook, requests) defers behind a new `initialize_runtime()` so the script can fast-exit without paying the import cost when there's nothing to do. (4) Per-book `refresh_cwa_session` + `invalidate_duplicate_cache` + `schedule_debounced_duplicate_scan` calls consolidate into a single `run_post_batch_follow_up()` that fires ONCE after the dirty-marker batch goes quiet — eliminates redundant per-book HTTP calls during sustained ingest. (5) New `_post_internal_endpoint()` helper retries the cwa-internal POSTs with timeouts and clearer failure logging instead of single-shot best-effort. **Reconciliation against fork-original work:** kept fork PR #199's `CalibreDB.refresh_for_new_data()` synchronous refresh in `/cwa-internal/reconnect-db` (going back to `TaskReconnectDatabase` via `WorkerThread.add` would re-introduce the engine-disposal race that caused fork #192); kept PR #199's `_run_calibredb_add_with_retry` + `metadata_db_write_lock()` at module top; kept PR #208's deferred lock-acquire pattern but routed it through @navels' `initialize_runtime()` to instantiate `process_lock` lazily; restored PR #37 / #56's `s6-setuidgid abc` privilege drop inside @navels' new `run_processor_with_timeout()` helper (without it the ingest worker would have regressed back to running as root). PR #210's `duplicate_scan_debounce_seconds` 30-default + 10-clamp tests for `ingest_processor.py` were updated to no-op since @navels' refactor moved the scheduling server-side via `/cwa-internal/queue-duplicate-scan` — equivalent gates still pinned at `cps/cwa_functions.py` + `cps/editbooks.py` + template-fallback sites. **Complementary to v4.0.66 PR #212** (UDF connect-listener) which eliminated the GIL+SQLite mutex deadlock vector fundamentally; this PR adds defense-in-depth by avoiding the race surface entirely (deferring duplicate-scan + DB reconnect until the batch is quiet) plus orthogonal ingest reliability (stale-event filtering, retry resilience). **6 new unit tests** in `tests/unit/test_ingest_batch_dirty.py` + `tests/unit/test_ingest_processor_startup.py` (batch dirty marker writes on success but not on failure, hot-loop HTTP calls suppressed, missing-target subprocess skip, optional cps module retry semantics) + **35 smoke tests** + **165 shell tests** for the s6 service. **Live container verification on cwn-local**: missing-target fast-exit (`python ingest_processor.py /tmp/nonexistent.epub`) returns 0 with `[ingest-processor] Skipping missing ingest target` logged + no runtime initialization + no lock acquired; post-batch follow-up (`--post-batch-follow-up`) acquires lock once, hits all three internal endpoints, returns 0; real ingest of `alice-in-wonderland.epub` triggers `[cwa-ingest-service] Post-batch follow-up triggered` and `[cwa-duplicates] Cache refreshed after after_import scan: groups=2 max_book_id=12` exactly once for the batch. | `f1ae6b18` | v4.0.74 |
| #266 | [#1074](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1074) | @SethMilliken | cwasync KOReader plugin: hide/disable Push and Pull menu actions when no document is currently open. Tapping "Push progress from this device now" or "Pull progress from other devices now" with no book loaded previously fired with `self.ui.document == nil`, producing silent failures because there was no current document to compute a checksum from. New `hasActiveDocument()` helper gates both menu items via their `enabled_func`, and the auto-sync toggle now short-circuits when no document is open. New `statusTextIfActionUnavailable()` appends a contextual `" (Password Not Set)"` or `" (No Active Document)"` suffix to the menu label so users can see *why* the action is unavailable instead of an unresponsive tap. | #350 | [#1344](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1344) | @shavitmichael | **Kobo sync requests are noticeably faster — roughly 15 seconds saved per sync round.** Four orthogonal optimizations in the Kobo sync hot path: (1) `generate_auth_token` no longer pre-converts kepubs by walking Kobo Sync shelves; conversion is deferred to `helper.get_download_link` and happens lazily when a Kobo actually requests `/download/<id>/kepub`, scoped to that single book, blocking (120s timeout) with EPUB fallback. (2) `KoboSyncState` and default `ReadingState` row creation deferred so the sync read isn't blocked by serialised writes. (3) Book metadata query that builds the sync payload now `joinedload`s authors / series / comments / languages — the per-book lazy-load fan-out in the metadata serializer is gone. (4) Single `downloadUrl` per book (was EPUB + EPUB3 + KEPUB); Kobo handles the EPUB fallback if kepub conversion fails. **Fork-side test updates** (no behaviour change to the cherry-pick): two existing source-pin tests had asserted the shape of the now-deleted auto-convert loop in `generate_auth_token` (fork pins for CWA #1328 blank-page lazy-load and CWA #817 unbounded library walk). The loop is gone in this design — kepub conversion still happens but at download time, scoped to the single book the device requests — which closes both regression vectors structurally rather than by defensive shape. Tests rewritten to pin the new design: `generate_auth_token` must not query `db.Books` or call `convert_book_format`; `get_download_link` must call `convert_book_format(book.id, ...)` gated on `config.config_kepubifypath` with `blocking=True`. `test_kobo_android_app_compat.py` had its `DrmType` pin broadened to the whole `cps.kobo` module so the dict-construction moving from inline into a `build_download_url` helper stays green. Greptile 4/5 confirmed safe to merge. | `27b334cc` | v4.0.146 |

| [#469](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/469) | [fork #465](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/465) / [CWA #1396](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1396) (@stuhby) | **Hardlinked files dropped into ingest subfolders were silently never imported.** A download client (Readarr / Bookshelf via qBittorrent) that hardlinks a completed file into a per-author subfolder of the ingest tree triggers only `IN_CREATE` — `link()` opens no file descriptor, so no `IN_CLOSE_WRITE` ever fires — and the inotify watcher in `cwa-ingest-service/run` listened only for `close_write` + `moved_to`, so those books were skipped until moved to the ingest root by hand. **Fix:** the watcher now also watches `-e create`; `handle_event` is event-type aware and ingests a CREATE only for a *completed hardlink* (`st_nlink > 1`, non-zero stable size), leaving a single-link in-progress download (`nlink == 1`) for its eventual `close_write` so partial files are never ingested; directory CREATEs are ignored via the regular-file check. **Verified:** 7 RED-on-main/GREEN tests driven through the real `bash` `handle_event` with a real `os.link` hardlink + static watch-line pin; live cwn-local end-to-end (hardlink in a subfolder ingested; new `$events` arg unbroken in the fallback watcher); `/security-review` clean (quoting airtight, filepath reaches Python only as a distinct `execve` argv). | [#482](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/482) | [fork #461](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/461) (@chloeroform) | **In-progress books with no language metadata vanished from the "Currently Reading" magic shelf while the book's own page still showed reading progress.** @chloeroform saw it split PDF-vs-EPUB on v4.0.161. **Root cause — read-path asymmetry, not the kosync writer:** the magic-shelf query (`cps/magic_shelf.py` `build_book_query_for_magic_shelf`) applies `CalibreDB.common_filters`, whose language clause `Books.languages.any(lang_code == user.filter_language())` fires whenever `default_language != "all"`. | #471 | [fork #470](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/470) (@sltvtr) | **The desktop Fetch-Metadata modal footer (the only "Close" button) stayed inside the viewport on long result lists.** @sltvtr reported on v4.0.164 (docker/x86) that the *Fetch Metadata* popup on the Edit Book page grew taller than the browser window, pushing the footer "Close" button off the bottom of the screen; zooming the page to 80% was the workaround. **Root cause:** the caliBlur theme already bounds the scrolling results region (`#meta-info` → `max-height: calc(100vh - 357px)`) and modal body, but it also pushes the whole dialog down — `padding-top: 60px` on `#metaModal` plus a `translateY(10%)` transform on the dialog (~90px on a 907px-tall dialog). | [#457](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/457) | [CW #3403](https://github.com/janeczku/calibre-web/issues/3403) | **Metadata edits no longer fail for authors whose names transliterate alike.** Editing any field of a book by an author like "George Pólya" (when "George Polya" also exists), or the Chinese homophones `姚尧`/`妖妖`, crashed with `(sqlite3.IntegrityError) UNIQUE constraint failed: authors.name` — even a cover-only edit. **Root cause:** the registered `lower` SQLite UDF is `unidecode.unidecode(s.lower())` (`cps/db.py`), which strips accents and transliterates; `prepare_authors` resolved the author via `func.lower(db.Authors.name).ilike(in_aut).first()`, so two distinct authors folded together and the unordered `.first()` picked the wrong twin, which `create_objects_for_addition` then renamed onto the submitted name → UNIQUE collision (autoflush). **Fix (`cps/editbooks.py`):** new pure `select_existing_author` helper resolves exact-name → true Unicode case-fold variant → first-candidate fallback, so a transliteration twin is never chosen for the rename path; legitimate casing/accent-correction renames preserved. | #399 | [fork #319 dup-series](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/319) data-safety (D3/D11) | **Resolving duplicates can no longer leave a phantom half-deleted book.** The auto-resolve loop deleted a duplicate's files (`helper.delete_book`) BEFORE committing the DB deletes (`delete_whole_book` + `calibre_db.session.commit`); a failure in between left the files gone but the `Books` row surviving — a ghost book that shows in the library and 404s on open, unrecoverable without the backup. **Fix:** DB-commit-first, files-last — a DB failure now leaves the book fully intact (files + rows) so the per-book except records an error and the duplicate stays resolvable next run; a post-commit file-cleanup failure is logged, not raised (row already gone; backup + orphaned files reclaimable). The files-last cleanup is handed a plain-value stand-in (`_DeletedBookFileRef`, id+path) instead of the ORM `book`, which `delete_whole_book`'s intermediate custom-column commits expire/detach (Greptile #399 catch — would raise `DetachedInstanceError` + orphan files on any custom-column library). **Verified:** 14/14 source pins (3 RED-on-main/GREEN); live cwn-local — clean run 6 losers removed, 0 errors, no DetachedInstanceError; injected DB-commit failure → loser row + files both intact (no phantom). /security-review clean. | #397 | [fork #319 dup-series](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/319) data-safety (D2) | **Resolving duplicates is safe even if a duplicate scan runs at the same moment.** `execute_resolution` (HTTP, gevent greenlet) and `TaskDuplicateScan` auto-resolve (a real OS worker thread — `gevent.monkey.patch_all` is not called) could both enter the destructive delete loop on the same group: double-delete, half-removed duplicate, or a transient error leaving the library inconsistent. **Fix:** a module-level `threading.Lock` serializes the `dry_run=False` resolution; acquired **non-blocking** (`acquire(blocking=False)`) so a contending caller declines cleanly with `in_progress` rather than parking the gevent hub greenlet and stalling every HTTP request (Greptile P2). Released once in `finally`. **Verified:** 5 RED-on-main/GREEN source pins; live two-real-thread A/B on cwn-local — fixed run: 6 clean deletes, contended thread declines "already in progress"; unfixed run: 4 errors + a book orphaned/duplicate persists. /security-review clean. | `93bc01a09` | v4.0.159 |
| #395 (+#396 guard `d6ce17c31`) | [fork #319 dup-series](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/319) data-safety (D7) | **Books that are *missing* a title or author are no longer grouped as duplicates of each other.** Two unrelated books that both had no title (or no author) collapsed into one "duplicate" group keyed on empty-string metadata — and could then be offered for deletion. **Fix:** incomplete-metadata books are excluded from grouping; #396 moved the guard onto the actual grouping/write path and corrected the author-presence check. **Verified:** RED-on-main/GREEN source pins + a behavioural distinct-keys test. /security-review clean. | `985aaacdf` | v4.0.159 |

| #389 | (operator audit — root cause behind the #320 default-theme display-bug class) | **caliBlur theme enforcement is now airtight; the deprecated default (light) theme can no longer leak through.** `admin.before_request` forced `g.current_theme = 1` only AFTER a block of unguarded `config.*` reads + a DB autoconfig/recovery block, and two `@app.before_request` handlers in `cps/__init__.py` run before it — any exception there left `g.current_theme` undefined, so templates (`{% if g.current_theme == 1 %}`) fell back to the deprecated default theme on the rendered (usually error) page. | #377 | (no tracker issue — root-caused from 3 silent 10-min CI freezes in 24h; same symptom class as upstream [CWA #1256](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1256)'s hub stall, which the #212 listener fix narrowed but did not close) | **The whole app can no longer freeze when a background task and a page load hit the database simultaneously.** AB-BA deadlock between the Python GIL and sqlite's per-connection mutex: serialized-mode sqlite (Linux builds, `threadsafety==3`) takes the connection mutex inside EVERY `sqlite3_*` call, including the short ones pysqlite makes GIL-held (`reset`/`bind`/`finalize`/`create_function`); a thread mid-`step` in a Python-UDF trampoline (mutex held, wants GIL) + any GIL-held short call (wants mutex) starves every thread in the process — pytest-timeout, xdist IPC, the gevent hub — until SIGKILL. Reachable in production: `WorkerThread`/APScheduler are real OS threads and 7 task modules (thumbnail, metadata_backup, duplicate_scan…) query the same StaticPool shared connection the web greenlets use. **Why it never reproduced on the dev machine:** macOS sqlite is multi-thread mode (`threadsafety==1`) — no connection mutex exists; the hammer ran 3000 iterations clean on macOS and froze at iteration 1 in a 2-CPU `python:3.13` container. Evidence: py-spy dump of the frozen process (GIL holder spinning in an adaptive pthread mutex; six threads parked on a FREE lock they can't take without the GIL), GIL-liveness heartbeat stopping at beat 1 — `notes/fix-udf-gil-deadlock-DESIGN.md` + `notes/udf-gil-deadlock-artifacts/`. **Fix:** `_SerializedSqliteConnection`/`_SerializedSqliteCursor` — per-connection RLock taken (GIL released while waiting) before every pysqlite C entry point, wired via `connect_args['factory']` into both calibre engines; `interrupt()` deliberately unwrapped (documented mutex-free-safe, must stay usable to break a stuck statement). **Verification (serialized build):** deterministic child-process red/green test — the unguarded control PROVABLY freezes (harness can't pass vacuously), the guarded path survives the exact interleave; 2000-iteration stampede hammer clean @160/s vs frozen-at-iteration-1 unpatched; the two previously-freezing concurrency tests now mirror production connect_args. CI hardening: `-o faulthandler_timeout=90` (faulthandler dumps all stacks WITHOUT the GIL — future freezes produce named stacks, not silent walls). Greptile's 3 P2s applied (hook registrars wrapped; arg-order-agnostic source pin; docstring). | `b10735026` | v4.0.157 |
| #376 | [fork #331](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/331) (@Gusdezup: "is there a plan to reduce the response header size on /v1/library/sync so it fits within nginx's default 4K buffer?") | **Kobo sync works behind reverse proxies with stock 4K buffers (Synology DSM, default nginx).** With Kobo store proxying on, the store's ~2-2.5KB JWT is embedded in our sync-token JSON and base64'd AGAIN (+33% on the largest component) → 4352B total response headers in the reporter-mirror repro → HTTP 502 through an nginx:alpine sidecar with default `proxy_buffer_size` while direct HTTP works ("Sync failed" on device). Our own cursor fields are only ~495B — the store token dominates. **Fix:** transport-level compression — `build_sync_token` emits `z1:` + b64(zlib(json)); `from_headers` sniffs the prefix and keeps parsing legacy plain-b64 tokens. Devices echo the token opaquely → zero device migration; `:` can't appear in b64 and `.` (kobo-store raw-token sentinel) can't appear in the prefix → no format collisions; schema VERSION untouched (transport, not schema). Decompression bounded (CWE-409): 16KB compressed pre-filter + 64KB `decompressobj(max_length)` cap + unconsumed-tail rejection; hostile/truncated/oversized tokens degrade to a fresh sync exactly like malformed legacy tokens (no 500 path — verified across 8 hostile-input classes). **Post-fix:** 3502B worst-case headers (high-entropy JWT budget pin — a run-of-'x' fixture compresses 10x and would pass trivially; real store JWTs are b64 of cryptographic material and barely compress) / 1158B typical; 200 through the same 4K proxy, cursor preserved, full magic-shelf sync clean. 12 unit tests; 324 kobo/synctoken green; simulator's decoder updated for `z1:`. | #369 | (Greptile follow-up review on [PR #368](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/368) — P sub-cursor stale-token re-injection after rebuild reset) | **The cache-rebuild reset of the magic-shelf sub-cursor actually persists to the next sync.** v4.0.154 introduced cache-rebuild detection that resets the LOCAL `magic_shelf_last_id` to `-1` when `magic_shelf_membership_added_at > sync_token.magic_shelf_membership_at`. Greptile noticed that the `new_magic_shelf_last_id` computation at the end of the loop still sourced from `sync_token.magic_shelf_last_id` (the stale persisted value) instead of the local variable. When a post-rebuild batch contains no magic books (e.g. it's full of regular books that sort before the magic ones in `(lm, id)` order), the else-branch silently overwrites the reset with the stale token value, `magic_shelf_membership_at` is advanced to match, and subsequent syncs no longer re-trigger the rebuild detection — leaving low-id magic books undelivered until another shelf modification. **Fix:** one-line correctness fix — both branches of `new_magic_shelf_last_id` (the `max()` advance branch and the no-magic-books else branch) source from the local `magic_shelf_last_id` variable so the rebuild-reset value propagates to the token write. **3 RED→GREEN AST-based tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_magic_shelf_use_local_sub_cursor_after_reset_368.py`: defense-in-depth pins against the specific buggy patterns (`max(sync_token.magic_shelf_last_id, ...)` and `new_magic_shelf_last_id = sync_token.magic_shelf_last_id`); positive AST assertion that the `max()` sources from the local variable. **456 Kobo+sync unit tests pass.** Live `cwn-local`: route returns HTTP 200. | `410427fa0` | v4.0.155 |
| #368 | (Greptile review on [PR #367](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/367) — P sub-cursor staleness across cache rebuilds) | **Kobo sync correctly resets the magic-shelf sub-cursor when the cache is rebuilt.** v4.0.153 persisted `magic_shelf_last_id` in the SyncToken across sync sessions to walk through large shelves. But if a sync ended with `cont_sync=False` on an exactly-full batch (book_count == SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT), the persisted `magic_shelf_last_id` sits at a high value (e.g. 149). If the user then adds a low-id book to the magic shelf and the cache rebuilds before the next sync, the arm filter `id IN magic_set AND id > magic_shelf_last_id` silently excludes the new book. The empty batch triggers `batch_drained`, fold fires, cursor advances past the new T_magic, and the book stays undelivered until ANOTHER cache rebuild lifts cache.created_at past the new cursor.lm. **Fix:** track `magic_shelf_membership_at` on the SyncToken (default `datetime.min`; VERSION 1-3-0 → 1-4-0; MIN_VERSION unchanged — pre-1-4-0 tokens parse cleanly and default the new field to min). At the start of each `HandleSyncRequest`, compare `magic_shelf_membership_added_at > sync_token.magic_shelf_membership_at`: if newer, reset `magic_shelf_last_id = -1` so the sub-cursor walk restarts from id=0. At end of request, persist `sync_token.magic_shelf_membership_at = max(stored, current)` so the next sync compares against the most-recent cache.created_at the device has seen. **6 RED→GREEN tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_magic_shelf_reset_on_cache_rebuild_367.py`: SyncToken field default + round-trip + pre-1-4-0 backward-compat; AST pin for the membership-at comparison in HandleSyncRequest; AST pin for the write-back; behavioral SQLite test reproducing Greptile's exact scenario (session 1 leaves magic_shelf_last_id=149; user adds id=10; cache rebuilds; session 2 delivers id=10). **453 Kobo+sync unit tests pass.** Live cwn-local: VERSION 1-4-0, magic_shelf_membership_at default = datetime.min, HTTP `/v1/library/sync` returns 200, both runtime markers present in deployed module. | `cc28e74f2` | v4.0.154 |
| #367 | (Greptile follow-up review on [PR #366](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/366) — P1 termination failure introduced by v4.0.152) | **Kobo sync no longer infinite-loops on magic shelves with >= SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT books.** v4.0.152's `batch_drained`-gated fold introduced a new correctness bug for large magic shelves: when `len(magic_shelf_book_ids) >= SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT` (100), the deferred fold never fires. The bare `id IN magic_shelf_book_ids` arm is cursor-unaware — it re-introduces ALL magic books on every round regardless of cursor position. Concrete failure (Greptile's scenario): 200 magic books at one T_bulk. Round 1: ORDER BY (lm, id) LIMIT 100 → ids 1-100; cursor → (T_bulk, 100). Round 2: query `(lm > T_bulk) OR (lm == T_bulk AND id > 100) OR (id IN {1..200})` → matches 200 books → ORDER BY (lm, id) LIMIT 100 yields ids 1-100 AGAIN. `batch_drained = False` every round; cursor never changes; `cont_sync = True` forever. **Fix:** add a magic-shelf sub-cursor. New SyncToken field `magic_shelf_last_id` (default -1; VERSION 1-2-0 → 1-3-0; MIN_VERSION unchanged for backward-compat — pre-1-3-0 tokens parse cleanly and default the new field to -1). The arm becomes `Books.id IN magic_shelf_book_ids AND Books.id > magic_shelf_last_id`. After each batch, advance `magic_shelf_last_id` to the max id of magic-shelf books emitted. When the fold fires (cursor advances past T_magic — cache.created_at window closed), reset `magic_shelf_last_id = -1` so the next cache rebuild starts walking the arm from id=0. With the fix: round 1 emits ids 1-100, sub-cursor=100; round 2 query becomes `... OR (id IN {1..200} AND id > 100)` → ids 101-200; round 3 finds nothing, fold fires, termination. **8 RED→GREEN tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_magic_shelf_sub_cursor_large_shelves.py` pin: arm shape (membership + sub-cursor + `magic_shelf_arm` name); sub-cursor sourced from sync_token; advance + reset + write back to token; behavioral SQLite test reproducing PRE-FIX infinite loop (200-book scenario; round 1 == round 2 output proves the bug) AND POST-FIX correctness (all 200 magic books deliver in ≤4 rounds; mixed 200 magic + 100 regular library delivers all 300). **5 new SyncToken tests** pin the field default, round-trip, pre-1-3-0 backward-compat, garbage-input defaults, presence in built data payload. VERSION pin relaxed to `>= 1-3-0`. **447 Kobo+sync unit tests pass.** Live cwn-local: VERSION 1-3-0, magic_shelf_last_id default -1, all 4 runtime markers present; HTTP `/v1/library/sync` returns 200 with v1-3-0 token shape; decoded token data carries `magic_shelf_last_id: -1` alongside the other fields on the wire. | `513bf1cad` | v4.0.153 |
| #366 | (Greptile review on [PR #361](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/361) — P1 correctness finding still present through v4.0.151) | **Magic-shelf fold no longer permanently drops pending regular books when batch is full.** Greptile's review on the v4.0.147 Kobo sync cursor PR surfaced a real correctness bug carried through v4.0.151: when `magic_shelf_arm_active=True` AND the sync batch is FULL (`len(books_list) == SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT`), the cursor fold unconditionally advances cursor to `magic_shelf_membership_added_at`. Any pending regular books whose `Books.last_modified` falls between the batch's max and T_magic are then permanently dropped on every subsequent sync (their lm < T_magic so composite_keyset fails; the magic-shelf arm gate `cache > cursor` goes False because cache no longer > cursor). **Concrete failure scenario** (Greptile's): 50 magic-shelf-only books + 100 regular shelf books, all at one T_bulk; cache fresh (T_magic > T_bulk); round 1 delivers first 100; v4.0.151 fold fires; cursor jumps to T_magic; round 2: 100 remaining regular books have `lm = T_bulk < T_magic`; none match any inner-cursor arm; **100 books permanently dropped**. **Fix:** defer the fold when batch is full. New gate `batch_drained = len(books_list) < SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT`. When batch is full the next round walks the remaining ties via the composite keyset; the magic-shelf arm stays active so already-emitted magic books may re-emit (idempotent on the device — bandwidth waste only, no data loss). Once pending books drain (batch < limit), fold fires, cursor jumps past T_magic, arm goes False, termination achieved. Also addresses the Greptile P2 finding: `books_last_id` reset to -1 alongside the early sync-token reset block (when KoboSyncedBooks is empty for the user) — harmless before because `lm > datetime.min` is True for every valid book, but keeps the two cursor components consistent for future readers. **5 RED→GREEN tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_magic_shelf_fold_defer_when_batch_full.py`: AST pin for the named `batch_drained` flag in the fold's outer if; AST-walk pin against bare `if magic_shelf_arm_active:` regression; behavioral SQLite test reproducing PRE-FIX (Greptile's exact 50+100 scenario; 50 regulars dropped) and POST-FIX (all 150 deliver in ≤5 rounds); termination test for magic-only collections. **277 Kobo unit tests pass.** Live `cwn-local`: route returns 200; both runtime markers (`batch_drained` flag, `sync_token.books_last_id = -1` reset) verified in deployed module. V2-track: magic books re-emitting during multi-round drainage is bandwidth waste; proper fix needs a `magic_shelf_last_id` sub-cursor for keyset pagination within the arm. | `06c147812` | v4.0.152 |
| #365 | (fork issue [#359](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/359) v4.0.147 follow-up, reporter @recruiterguy) | **Magic-shelf books now deliver in sync-all-library mode too — closing the v4.0.147 gap.** @recruiterguy verified v4.0.147 deployed cleanly but reported magic-shelf books still don't deliver; their diagnostic showed `magic_shelf_cache.created_at` still at 2026-06-04 (unchanged across 5 post-deploy sync requests). **Root cause:** their user has `current_user.kobo_only_shelves_sync=False` (sync-all-library mode). (2) Split `inner_cursor_filter` into `inner_cursor_filter_with_bookshelf` (only_kobo_shelves branch: composite keyset + `BookShelf.date_added` arm from #220 + magic-shelf arm) and `inner_cursor_filter_sync_all` (else branch: composite keyset + magic-shelf arm; drops `date_added` since that branch doesn't join BookShelf and referencing it would SQL-error). (3) The deletion-detection block (synced_book_ids minus allowed_book_ids) stays gated on `kobo_only_shelves_sync` — that logic is specifically for the outer-membership-filter case; in sync-all mode the user wants every book on the device. **5 new AST-based tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_magic_shelf_sync_all_mode_359.py` pin: helper calls are NOT inside `kobo_only_shelves_sync` block; unconditional calls exist at function scope; sync-all branch uses the new filter; sync-all filter doesn't reference `BookShelf.date_added`; only_kobo_shelves filter keeps it; deletion-detection stays gated. | #361 | (fork issues [#347](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/347), reporters @andree392 + @shavitmichael + @Glennza1962, and [#359](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/359), reporter @recruiterguy) | **Two faces of one defect: the Kobo sync cursor was missing arms.** #347 — full sync never finishes when >SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT books share one `Books.last_modified` (classic bulk-import signature; @andree392's library had 4458 books all stamped 2021-03-29 13:31:44). The device's "My Books" counter climbed past 5000+ while the server re-sent the same first 50 books forever; debug log: `changed entries: 4458 / selected to sync: 50 / remaining: 4458` repeating. **#359** — Magic Shelves marked `kobo_sync=1` never delivered, even with `magic_shelf_cache` populated. The inner cursor (`last_modified > token` OR `date_added > token`) ran before the outer `(kobo_sync shelf OR magic-shelf)` filter; magic-shelf-only books had NULL `BookShelf.date_added` (not in `book_shelf_link`) and old `last_modified`, so both arms returned false and the rows were excluded before the outer membership filter saw them. **Root cause for both:** `HandleSyncRequest`'s ORDER BY is `(last_modified, id)` but the cursor was `books_last_modified` alone — no id tiebreaker. The PR #213 / CWA #1351 (@raphi011) constraint had to be preserved: adding `magic_shelf_book_ids` unconditionally to the inner OR causes an infinite `cont_sync` loop. **Fix:** `SyncToken` gains `books_last_id` (default `-1`); `VERSION` bumped `1-1-0` → `1-2-0`; `MIN_VERSION` stays `1-0-0` so devices on older tokens parse cleanly without forced re-sync (`id > -1` is True for every valid book id, so no books at exactly `cursor_lm` are dropped on the first post-upgrade sync). Both cursor sites use a composite keyset `(last_modified > cursor_lm) OR (last_modified == cursor_lm AND id > cursor_id)` — standard keyset pagination on ORDER BY `(lm, id)`. The magic-shelf branch gains a third inner-OR arm `Books.id IN magic_shelf_book_ids` gated on `MagicShelfCache.created_at > cursor_lm`; the cursor folds `magic_shelf_membership_added_at` into `new_books_last_modified` so the arm goes False on the next sync (preserves the #213 termination guarantee structurally). `new_books_last_id` resets to `-1` when the cursor is pushed past the batch's max book ts via the #220 `date_added` fold or the #359 `magic_shelf_cache` fold. `changed_entries` batch materialized once into `books_list` (was double-queried). **26 RED→GREEN tests** (`tests/unit/test_kobo_synctoken_books_last_id.py` — 11 pinning the field, default, round-trip, backward-compat with pre-`1-2-0` tokens, garbage-input defaults, VERSION/MIN_VERSION; `tests/unit/test_kobo_sync_composite_keyset_cursor.py` — 15 pinning the inline-query composition, magic-shelf arm gate, `books_last_id` cursor write, batch materialization, and a real-SQLite behavioral test that reproduces the pre-fix 150-book drop on a 250-book collision and proves the post-fix exhaustively walks @andree392's 4458-book collision in <=90 batches). 423 kobo/sync unit tests pass. **Live `cwn-local` verification:** HTTP `/v1/library/sync` returns 200 with v1-2-0 token carrying `books_last_id`; follow-up sync with the returned token does not re-emit the previously-delivered book (cursor advance correct); no errors in container logs; runtime markers confirmed `composite_keyset_books_only`, `inner_cursor_filter`, `magic_shelf_arm_active`, `sync_token.books_last_id = new_books_last_id`, `get_magic_shelf_membership_added_at` all present in the loaded module. Adjacency v2-track: reading-state cursor + archive cursor share the trap class but have much lower collision likelihood; magic-shelf collections > SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT books need a `magic_shelf_last_id` sub-cursor — see `notes/fix-kobo-sync-composite-keyset-347-359-adjacency.md`. | `180bce4db` | v4.0.147 |

| #356 | (community PR by @sarsey-walker) | **Three bundled hardening fixes: Hardcover auto-fetch session stability, "Use via HTTPS" config persistence, and TLS-aware container healthcheck.** (1) **Hardcover auto-fetch**: long scans could fail with detached-ORM-instance errors and contaminate the global `ub.session` from a background worker thread (poisoning later web requests). The task now queries book IDs (not full `Books` objects), re-fetches each book in its own short-lived scope inside `_process_book`, and never reaches into `ub.session` from the worker. Avoids the N+1 reload regression from an earlier fix attempt. (2) **"Use via HTTPS" persistence**: the admin toggle existed in the model and the UI but the Basic Configuration save handler never persisted it. Saving now writes the checkbox state, and `apply_https_runtime_config` re-applies the cookie-security flags to the running process so the change takes effect without a restart. The shared helper is the single source of truth — used at boot and after every save. (3) **TLS-aware container healthcheck**: when CWA serves HTTPS directly via cert/key, the previous HTTP probe spammed `Gevent SSL Error: [SSL: HTTP_REQUEST]`. The new `/usr/local/bin/cwa-healthcheck` helper reads the configured cert/key from `app.db`; if both files exist on disk it probes `https://` with `-k` (the cert is the server's own and curl has no CA trust for it); otherwise stays on `http://`. The HEALTHCHECK CMD invariants the existing tests pinned (`/health` target, `CWA_PORT_OVERRIDE` default 8083, bounded `--connect-timeout` 1s + `--max-time` 2s) are preserved — they just moved from inline curl to the helper script. `tests/unit/test_dockerfile_healthcheck.py` now inspects the union of both files so the same invariants stay enforced wherever they live. | `6bb68457` | v4.0.146 |
| #355 | (fork issue [#354](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/354), reporter @Neuromancien59) | **The admin Configuration page stops returning 500 after a long-running upgrade.** Reporter on Debian/x86 v4.0.144 hit `GET /admin/config` → HTTP 500 (`UndefinedError: No first item, sequence was empty`) with startup log `Failed to initialize OAuth blueprints: no such column: oauthProvider.oauth_authorize_url`. **Root cause** (`cps/ub.py:1386` — `migrate_oauth_provider_table`): the migration probed one column (`oauth_base_url`) as a stand-in for its five-column group and added the group only if that probe threw, so a DB with `oauth_base_url` present but the rest of the group missing — the exact partial state a multi-release upgrade produces — passed the probe and the missing columns were never added. The second column group (`metadata_url` proxying for `scope`/`username_mapper`/`email_mapper`/`login_button`) had the same shape, and both ALTERs ran as one all-or-nothing batch. OAuth init then failed on the missing column at boot, `oauth_bb.oauthblueprints` was left empty, and `config_edit.html` did `provider \| selectattr(...) \| first` on the empty sequence → 500. **Fix:** rewrite the migration to introspect the live schema with `sa_inspect` and ADD only the columns actually missing, one ALTER per statement, tolerating `duplicate column name` per column so a concurrent gunicorn-worker boot can't abort the loop mid-way. `config_edit.html` falls back to `{}` when no generic provider is configured (`(... \| first) or {}`) so the page renders even if OAuth init ever leaves the list empty (defense-in-depth — once the migration is fixed the list is populated, but the page should never 500 on an empty list regardless of the cause). **6 regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_354_oauth_provider_migration.py` (real in-memory SQLite engines) pin partial-group-1 repair, partial-group-2 repair, double-run idempotency, all-old-schema repair, all-new-schema no-op, and the duplicate-column mid-loop race — the first three RED on `main` and GREEN on this branch (matching the reporter's exact error string). Adjacency: `migrate_user_session_table` shares the probe-by-proxy shape but the partial-state trigger is structurally closed there (both columns landed in the same upstream commit); documented as v2-track in `notes/fix-354-adjacency.md`. | `1ad232e8` | v4.0.145 |

| #344 | (fork issue [#343](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/343), reporter @Oakwhisper) | **Book covers overlapped the title text on Safari (main books grid).** On Safari/WebKit — desktop AND mobile — the covers on the books grid overlapped the title (no spacing between cover-bottom and title-top) and the hover-shading overlay looked misaligned; Chromium rendered correctly. **Root cause**: the cover anchor `#books > .cover > a` (+ `#books_rand` / `.isotope-item` variants) is `display: inline-block` with no `vertical-align`, so it defaults to `baseline`. | #132 | (audit 2026-05-11, item B2) | Kobo reading-state race: two concurrent PUTs to `/v1/library/<uuid>/state` from the same device (legitimately happens on wake-from-sleep) could race past the read-then-write check in `get_or_create_reading_state` and both INSERT, leaving duplicate `(user_id, book_id)` rows. The next `.one_or_none()` then raised `MultipleResultsFound` → 500 to the device, which retries forever. Two-part fix: (1) `UniqueConstraint(user_id, book_id)` added to `ReadBook`, `KoboReadingState`, `KoboSyncedBooks`, `ArchivedBook` (model + `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` via a new `migrate_kobo_unique_constraints` migration that dedupes existing duplicates with sensible winner rules — newest LM wins for KoboReadingState, status-level + LM for ReadBook, archived-wins for ArchivedBook — reparents KoboReadingState's bookmark/statistics children into the winner, sums `times_started_reading` across ReadBook losers so the user's read counter is preserved); (2) `get_or_create_reading_state` rewritten to `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT(user_id, book_id) DO NOTHING` via the sqlite dialect, so the race can't produce a duplicate even before the DB constraint trips. Migration is gated by a marker file in `CONFIG_DIR/.cwa_migrations/` so it runs at most once per install. 29 regression tests pin: model constraints declared, UNIQUE index enforced, dedupe rules per table, child reparenting, bookmark merge, idempotent marker behavior, concurrent-insert threaded test (16 threads, exactly one row), source-pin AST that `get_or_create_reading_state` uses `sqlite_insert + on_conflict_do_nothing` and not the legacy `.one_or_none()`. | `de2bd2e3` | v4.0.45 |
| #133 | (audit 2026-05-11, item B4) | Kobo per-callsite `common_filters` policy on `get_book_by_uuid`. Upstream's `calibre_db.get_book_by_uuid` bypasses `common_filters`, so the Kobo blueprint was handing back books the user's web UI would have hidden (denied-tagged, language-filtered, custom-column-restricted, or per-user-hidden via PR #105). Five callsites in `cps/kobo.py` audited; new helper `get_book_by_uuid_for_kobo(uuid, *, enforce_policy)` on `CalibreDB` makes the policy explicit. ENFORCE on the two policy-boundary surfaces (`HandleMetadataRequest` GET, `add_items_to_shelf`) — denied/hidden books shouldn't expose metadata via Kobo or leak onto a shared kobo-synced shelf. DO NOT enforce on device-trailing or destructive user-initiated surfaces (`HandleStateRequest` GET/PUT, `HandleTagRemoveItem`, `HandleBookDeletionRequest`) — reading-state must keep syncing for already-on-device books even if they later become denied, and cleanup operations must never block. `allow_show_archived=True` on the enforced path because `ArchivedBook` doubles as the Kobo's device-deletion track. | #137 | (fork issue [#121](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/121), reporter @droM4X, tested on Readest) | Three independent OPDS bugs. **(1) Log spam:** every OPDS catalogue fetch logged `OPDS Login failed for user ""` at WARN because clients commonly issue an unauthenticated probe before sending creds. `verify_password` now short-circuits on empty username — no DB query, no WARN. Real auth failures still log normally. **(2) Anon+auth multiplexing:** when anonymous browsing was enabled and the client sent stale credentials, the server returned 401 instead of falling back to the Guest catalog. `requires_basic_auth_if_no_ano` now retries with the synthetic Guest credentials when the first attempt fails AND `config.config_anonbrowse` is on. Auth-only deployments keep their 401 behavior unchanged. **(3) Three OPDS root labels rendered in English on translated UIs:** "Alphabetical Books", "Recently added Books", "Magic Shelves" — `OPDS_ROOT_ENTRY_DEFS` held bare Python literals so pybabel-extract never picked them up. Every title + description now wrapped with `N_()` (`flask_babel.lazy_gettext`); next extract cycle lands them in `messages.pot`. Existing translations for the older entries unchanged. 7 regression tests pin all three fixes including a behavioral mock asserting `log.warning` is never called for the empty-username probe. | `0edf8414` | v4.0.46 |

| #174 | (fork issue [#162](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/162), reporter @magdalar) | **Nightly `processed_books/fixed_originals/*.zip` written as `root:root` instead of `PUID:PGID`**. The `cwa-auto-zipper` s6 longrun service called `python3 /app/calibre-web-automated/scripts/auto_zip.py` directly while every other periodic service (`cwa-ingest-service`, `cwa-checksum-backfill`, `cwa-preview-cache-cleanup`) wraps its application Python with `s6-setuidgid abc`. The `.epub` files in the same directory landed correctly under PUID:PGID because they come from `cwa-ingest-service`, which already drops privileges. Fix is a one-line wrap of the loop's auto_zip.py invocation with `s6-setuidgid abc`. New `tests/unit/test_s6_service_privilege_drop.py` source-pins the regression (negative test verified — fails on the pre-fix line). End-to-end reproduced inside `cwn-local`: ran `auto_zip.py` against a /tmp test tree first as root (produces `root:root` zip) and then under `s6-setuidgid abc` (produces `abc:dialout` zip, mapping to PUID=501 PGID=20). Bind-mounted `/config` couldn't be used for the live test because Docker Desktop on macOS squashes virtiofs ownership to root regardless of process uid — `/tmp` (container layer) bypasses that quirk and exercises the real privilege-drop. Broader audit of similar services tracked in `notes/s6-privilege-drop-audit.md` (e.g. `metadata-change-detector` is structurally root-elevated but `cover_enforcer.py` chowns its own outputs — needs per-service analysis, not bundled here). | `84a7c0ba` | v4.0.55 |
| #167 | (fork issue [#147](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/147), reporter @iroQuai) | **Container won't start on v4.0.49+, gevent_wsgi NoneType crash**. `cps/gevent_wsgi.py` overrides `pywsgi.WSGIHandler.format_request` (introduced upstream in commit `1d7dcce98d`, 2024-07; byte-identical in our codebase across v4.0.44–v4.0.53). gevent calls `format_request` for *all* requests including those that fail HTTP parsing — TLS ClientHello on the plain-HTTP port (Traefik v3 sending TLS bytes), malformed headers, etc. For those, `get_environ()` is never invoked, so `self.environ` stays `None` and `self.environ.get(...)` raises `AttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'get'`. The reporter's "worked on .44, broke on .49" memory turned out to be partial — what changed in their environment was either healthcheck probe frequency or the Dockerfile `HEALTHCHECK`'s `https://localhost:8083` TLS fallback starting to fire, not anything in our code. Fix is a one-line None guard on `self.environ.get(...)`. New `tests/unit/test_gevent_wsgi_format_request.py` pins the 4 cases (environ=None → client_address fallback, X-Forwarded-For present, empty environ, all-None edge). Live repro on cwn-local: `printf '\x16\x03\x01\x00\x05hello\n' \| nc localhost 8086` produced the exact traceback before the fix; post-fix returns HTTP 400 with no traceback. Stress: 30 parallel TLS-bytes requests → 0 tracebacks, container stays healthy. Cold restart healthy in 7s. | `126f22aa` | v4.0.54 |

| #199 | (fork issue [#192](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/192), reporter @magdalar; same class as upstream CWA [#1082](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1082)) | **Concurrent auto-import of large epubs on `NETWORK_SHARE_MODE=true` crashed the web service to persistent 404s, required `docker compose restart`.** Four contributors, each addressed: (1) post-ingest `/cwa-internal/reconnect-db` enqueued `TaskReconnectDatabase` via `WorkerThread` — the worker disposed the shared SQLAlchemy engine while in-flight request greenlets were using it. Replaced with a synchronous `CalibreDB.refresh_for_new_data()` classmethod that expires loaded objects + rolls back the held read transaction across every instance; engine is never touched. (2) No application-level coordination between the Flask app and the `ingest_processor` subprocess on `metadata.db` writes. SQLite's fcntl locks are unreliable on mergerfs / SMB / NFS / Docker Desktop virtiofs. New `cps/services/calibre_db_lock.py` exposes a process-shared advisory flock at `/config/.cwa-metadata-write.lock` (local Docker volume, always supports flock). Applied around `calibre_db.session.commit()` in `editbooks.do_edit_book` and around `calibredb add` in `ingest_processor.add_book_to_library`. (3) `setup_db` + `check_valid_db` did not set `PRAGMA busy_timeout`; SQLAlchemy's `connect_args timeout=30` only applies at connect time. Added explicit `PRAGMA busy_timeout=60000`. (4) `calibredb add` failure was terminal — first transient lock moved the book to `/processed_books/failed`. New `_run_calibredb_add_with_retry` detects `'database is locked'` / `'BusyError'` in stderr and retries 4 attempts with 2s/4s/8s exponential backoff; non-lock errors surface immediately. **13 RED→GREEN regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_metadata_db_write_coordination.py` including a two-Python-process subprocess test of the flock cross-process semantics. | #210 | (fork issue [#134](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/134), reporter @Onkeyuk; follow-up trace by @kanjieater, CWA [#1256](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1256) original reporter; regression vector identified by @navels) | **Web UI 504s under sustained ingest on large libraries (~10k+ books) — default duplicate-scan debounce was too aggressive.** CWA upstream commit `fe60df7` (2026-01-29) lowered `duplicate_scan_debounce_seconds` from 30 → 5 to make duplicate-detection notifications appear faster after multi-book ingest. For users with 10k+ book libraries the 5s default produces stacking SQL prefilter queries (`find_duplicate_candidate_ids_sql`) that contend for the GIL with concurrent SQLAlchemy session-init paths (which call `conn.create_function` to register the `title_sort`/`lower` UDFs on the SQLite connection). The collision deadlocks the gevent hub. Default reverted to 30 in all five mirrored sites — schema literal (`scripts/cwa_schema.sql`), three Python fallbacks (`cps/cwa_functions.py` web process, `cps/editbooks.py`, `scripts/ingest_processor.py`), and the Jinja template fallback (`cps/templates/cwa_settings.html`). Runtime lower-bound clamp raised from 5 → 10 across all three clamp sites so users typing 5 through the admin UI get clamped to 10. One-time DB migration `_migrate_duplicate_debounce_5_to_30_v1` in `scripts/cwa_db.py`'s `CWA_DB.__init__` bumps existing installs from 5 → 30 once, gated by a marker file in `CONFIG_DIR/.cwa_migrations/duplicate_debounce_5_to_30_v1.applied`. Users who customised the value to anything other than 5 (e.g. 15, 60, 120) are not touched. 13 regression tests in `tests/unit/test_duplicate_debounce_default_regression.py` pin the schema literal, four Python fallbacks, three clamp sites, fresh-install behaviour, three migration variants (5 → 30, 15 preserved, 60 preserved), and the marker-idempotency contract. Live-verified on cwn-local: pre-restart DB had `duplicate_scan_debounce_seconds=5`; post-restart DB shows 30 + marker written; second restart is a no-op. Runtime clamp endpoint POST `delay_seconds=3` returns 10 (floor), `delay_seconds=700` returns 600 (ceiling), no delay returns 30 (default). Playwright UI pilot on `/cwa-settings` shows `value=30, min=10, max=600` with no console errors. This is a tactical regression revert — the underlying GIL+SQLite deadlock pattern still exists, just much less likely to trip under default settings. The architectural fixes live in upstream CWA PRs [#1349](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1349) (defer post-import reconnect + duplicate-cache invalidation until batch settles) and [#1353](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1353) (incremental duplicate index) and will be evaluated in follow-up cycles. | `71c799b5` | v4.0.65 |
| #212 | (fork issue [#134](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/134) follow-up to v4.0.65; root cause behind CWA [#1256](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1256)) | **Root-cause fix for the GIL+SQLite deadlock vector.** v4.0.65 reduced the collision frequency (debounce 5 → 30); this release eliminates the deadlock pattern structurally by moving `conn.create_function()` out of every request-handler hot path. With `StaticPool` sharing one SQLite connection across all threads, the pre-fix code called `create_functions` mid-request from `cps/web.py:get_matching_tags` (tag autocomplete — extremely frequent), `cps/editbooks.py` ×2 (edit-book entry + after format upload), `cps/admin.py:912` (admin config save when `config_title_regex` changes), `cps/helper.py:364` (set_read_status), `cps/search.py:250`, plus three internal db.py hot paths (`get_typeahead`, `check_exists_book`, `search_query`) and `init_session` for every new SQLAlchemy session. Each call held the GIL while invoking SQLite's C `create_function` — concurrent worker thread mid-`func.lower` query needed the GIL to invoke the UDF, and SQLite's connection mutex blocked both threads. New module-level `_register_sqlite_udfs(dbapi_connection, _connection_record)` in `cps/db.py` registers `lower`/`uuid4`/`title_sort` once via SQLAlchemy `event.listen(engine, 'connect', ...)` — wired on both `check_engine` (in `check_valid_db`) and the main `cls.engine` (in `setup_db`). `title_sort` reads `CalibreDB.config.config_title_regex` via closure at call time, so admin updates to the regex take effect on the next call without re-registration; the admin route at `cps/admin.py:912` now calls `db.CalibreDB.update_config(config)` to propagate the new regex without touching connection state. All 6 request-handler callsites + 3 internal db.py hot paths + the `init_session` call removed. `create_functions(self, config=None)` preserved as a backward-compat no-op shim. `title_sort` hardened: returns `''` on `NULL`, falls back to `strip_whitespaces` on malformed regex, never raises. 29 new regression tests across `tests/unit/test_sqlite_udf_registration_listener.py` (17 — source-pin every callsite removed, behavioural verification UDFs work without explicit registration, title_sort closure adapts to live config, concurrency smoke with 32 + 16 mixed threads) and `tests/unit/test_duplicate_debounce_migration_edge_cases.py` (12 — boundary value parametrised, empty table handling, marker write failure non-fatal, two concurrent CWA_DB constructors converge to 30, init-order pin). Live-verified on a fresh `cwng-udf-verify` container based on v4.0.65 image with patches applied via `docker cp`: 50 concurrent `/get_matching_tags` requests during an active duplicate scan all returned HTTP 200 in 1 second total, log scan shows the cwa-duplicates SQL prefilter ran cleanly with no "database is locked", no "no such function", no traceback. The deadlock vector is now structurally absent — no production code path calls `conn.create_function()` on a hot path. | `7b31d7e1` | v4.0.66 |
| #215 | (fork issue [#147](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/147) third gap; reporter @iroQuai persistence) | **Container falsely reported HEALTHY by Docker / k8s / Compose when the Calibre library was unmounted, empty, or unreadable.** The Dockerfile HEALTHCHECK probes `/health` with `curl -fsS`, but `admin.before_request` was 302-redirecting `/health` to `/admin/db_configuration` whenever `config.db_configured` was False — `curl -fsS` does not treat 3xx as failure, so the probe exited 0 and orchestration never paged on-call, never rolled back, never failed over. | #213 | [#1351](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1351) | @raphi011 | **Kobo multi-device sync: books synced on one device became invisible to other devices on the same Calibre-Web account.** `HandleSyncRequest` was filtering changed entries through the user-keyed `KoboSyncedBooks` table — once any device had synced a book, the filter excluded it from subsequent sync responses to any device on the same account. Per-device sync state lives in the `x-kobo-synctoken` cursor (the `last_modified` timestamp comparisons), so filtering by user-keyed sync table was both incorrect (locked out additional devices) and redundant. Also removed the `magic_shelf_book_ids` injection from the inner OR — that path bypassed the timestamp cursor and produced an infinite `cont_sync` loop on paginated sync. Magic-shelf membership is still correctly enforced by the OUTER filter (`kobo_sync` shelf OR magic-shelf) further down. | #227 | (operator pain report 2026-05-17 + live MITM capture against book UUID `0b800030-997b-4d71-9a1d-0d162c26c867`; companion to #226 B1/B2/B4 cluster) | **Books deleted from CW persisted on Kobo devices forever — the operator manually long-pressed → archived them on the device every time the library changed.** Wire-confirmed during the borrow-day capture: the reading-state handler kept firing `redirect_or_proxy_request()` every sync for the orphan book. **Root cause:** the Kobo protocol needs a book's UUID to address a `DeletedEntitlement` to the device, but `editbooks.delete_whole_book` destroyed the calibre `metadata.db` row (line 1394 pre-fix) before any sync handler could capture the UUID, and `kobo_synced_books` only stored `(user_id, book_id)`. The device interpreted absence-from-sync-response as "still on device, nothing changed," not as deletion. **Fix has four parts.** (1) New `ub.KoboDeletedBook` tombstone table — `(user_id, book_uuid, deleted_at)` snapshot with `UNIQUE(user_id, book_uuid)` for idempotent capture + `(user_id, deleted_at)` index for the sync query path. (2) `migrate_kobo_deleted_book` migration in `cps/ub.py` — creates the table if missing, gated by `CONFIG_DIR/.cwa_migrations/kobo_deleted_book_v1` marker; idempotent on re-run via `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` regardless of marker state. (3) `kobo_sync_status.record_book_deletion(book_id, book_uuid)` — enumerates affected users via `KoboSyncedBooks`, inserts per-user tombstones, clears the stale `KoboSyncedBooks` rows so the two-way deletion logic doesn't trip over them. No-op on missing UUID (defensive); idempotent per `(user_id, book_uuid)` via the UNIQUE. Called from `editbooks.delete_whole_book` BEFORE any metadata row is touched (also covers `delete_book_from_table` since that calls through to `delete_whole_book`). Wrapped in try/except so a tombstone-capture failure can't block the user's delete action — worst case is pre-fix orphan behavior, no data loss. (4) `HandleSyncRequest` emits `{"DeletedEntitlement": {"BookEntitlement": {"Id": uuid, "RevisionId": uuid, "CrossRevisionId": uuid}}}` for tombstones where `deleted_at > sync_token.archive_last_modified` (the device's cursor, NOT the local `new_archived_last_modified` which would mask legitimate tombstones whose `deleted_at` lies between the cursor and the local watermark). Advances `new_archived_last_modified` past each emitted tombstone so each device sees each one exactly once. Paginates via `SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT` + `cont_sync` so mass-deletes don't blow past the device's response cap. **15 regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_deleted_book_tombstone.py` — source-pinned (model + UNIQUE + migration wired into `migrate_Database` + helper exists + `delete_whole_book` calls it + sync emits `DeletedEntitlement` filtered against device cursor); behavioral SQLite (`record_book_deletion` creates per-affected-user tombstones not cross-user, idempotent on double-invocation, no-ops on missing UUID, clears stale `KoboSyncedBooks` rows); sync emission (pending rows in `deleted_at` order, cursor advance prevents re-emit on second sync, user_id filter prevents cross-user leak); migration (creates table from blank schema, marker written, second run no-op). **Live container verification:** cwn-local rebuilt from this branch — migration ran on cold boot (table + indexes + marker present in `/config/`); manually inserted tombstone for `cwng84test` user surfaced as 1 `DeletedEntitlement` with `{Id, RevisionId, CrossRevisionId}` all set to tombstone UUID alongside normal sync entitlements; returned synctoken had `archive_last_modified` advanced to tombstone's `deleted_at`; second sync with returned token returned 0 `DeletedEntitlement` (cursor correct, no re-emit); no new ERROR/WARN/Traceback in container logs. Closes the B3 portion of `notes/KOBO-BUG-CLUSTER-PROMPT-2026-05-17.md`. Design doc that informed this PR: `notes/B3-kobo-deleted-book-tombstone-DESIGN.md`. | `4daccbb5` | v4.0.71 |
| #226 | (fork issue [#220](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/220), reporter @Hoite; 2026-05-17 live MITM capture against a Libra Colour FW 4.45.23684) | **Three live-captured Kobo sync bugs sharing one anti-pattern — sync contract emits absences instead of tombstones, and sibling handlers reply 404 to unknown items so the device retries forever.** **B1 — ghost-shelf 404 retry loop:** `HandleTagUpdate` (`/v1/library/tags/<id>` DELETE/PUT) and `HandleTagRemoveItem` both `abort(404)` when the shelf is unknown unless `config_kobo_proxy` is on. | #248 | (community contribution by [@ikerios](https://github.com/ikerios); complementary to fork [#220](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/220) cursor-advance fix in v4.0.54) | **Kobo Forma stuck in infinite sync loop after factory reset and re-registration** — ~3 sync requests per second sustained for 15+ hours against a 393-book library, with `kobo_synced_books` fully populated and a recent device-side cursor. Each response carried 2 rows yet emitted `x-kobo-sync: continue`, so the device refused to persist the advanced synctoken and re-requested the same data forever. **Root cause** in `cps/kobo.py:HandleSyncRequest`: the books branch set `cont_sync = bool(book_count)` — True for any non-zero count. The Kobo protocol treats `x-kobo-sync: continue` as a paging signal ("more pages exist, keep your cursor pinned"), not a freshness signal. When the current batch is exhaustive (`book_count <= SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT`), emitting `continue` is a contract violation: the firmware suppresses synctoken persistence, the device re-requests with the same cursor, the server returns the same rows with `continue`, and the loop self-perpetuates. The reading-states branch seventeen lines below already used the correct `cont_sync \|= bool(changed_reading_states.count() > SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT)`. **Fix**: one-character semantic correction at line 353 — `bool(book_count)` → `bool(book_count > SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT)` to mirror the reading-states branch. **4 RED→GREEN regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_cont_sync_batch_cap.py` source-pin both branches use the `> SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT` shape; explicitly forbid the broken `cont_sync = bool(book_count)` pattern; cover the books-branch + reading-states-branch + all-bool-count-sites invariant. 194/194 kobo-touched unit tests pass. **Distinct from but complementary to fork #220**: that PR fixed the cursor-advance side (`BookShelf.date_added` folded into `new_books_last_modified`); this PR fixes the signal side. Both are required for `else`-branch users (no `kobo_only_shelves_sync`) to escape the loop. **Bug pre-dates the fork** — `git blame` points to upstream `janeczku/calibre-web`, so this is also a candidate for upstream backport. Live verification on cwn-local: code loads, source inspection confirms both `cont_sync = bool(...)` and `cont_sync \|= bool(...)` sites carry the `> SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT` comparison; the third `cont_sync = True` site is correctly guarded by an outer `if len(pending_deletions) >= SYNC_ITEM_LIMIT` block (tombstone-pagination, intentional). Credit @ikerios for the 15-hour production trace and the upstream-mirror fix structure. | `1ce7c60e` | v4.0.89 |

| #249 | (fork issue [#217](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/217), reporter @sjthespian) | **Metadata-search "Fetch Metadata" failed to find any book whose title contained an apostrophe** — reporter typed `At Winter's End`, got zero results; same title without the apostrophe returned the book on the first hit. Affected every provider whose URL-encodes the user-typed query: the ASCII apostrophe became `%27` and catalog indexes (Amazon, Google, Kobo, OpenLibrary, etc.) store the apostrophe-free form. **Root cause has two halves.** (1) `cps/services/Metadata.py:get_title_tokens` didn't normalize apostrophes — it stripped most punctuation but the apostrophe class survived through to URL encoding. (2) `cps/metadata_provider/amazon.py:178` passed the raw `query` directly into Amazon's `field-keywords` parameter, never invoking `get_title_tokens`, so even after fixing the tokenizer Amazon would still have shipped `Alice%27s+Adventures` to amazon.com/s. **Fix.** New first regex `r"['‘’ʼ`´]"` → `""` (strip, not space-replace, to keep `Don't` → `Dont` as one token) covering ASCII U+0027, curly U+2018/U+2019, modifier-letter U+02BC (Hawaiian okina), backtick U+0060, acute U+00B4. | #250 | (fork issue [#193](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/193); backports the first two commits of [@FRaccie](https://github.com/FRaccie)'s downstream [FRaccie/Calibre-Web-NextGen#1](https://github.com/FRaccie/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/1)) | **Container went unhealthy and `/duplicates` crashed on large libraries** with `sqlite3.OperationalError: too many SQL variables`. Symptom reported by @FRaccie on a ~200k-book production library; the duplicate prefilter returned ~170,231 candidate IDs and `find_duplicate_books_python` issued `db.Books.id.in_(list(candidate_ids))` as a single statement — exceeding SQLite's `SQLITE_MAX_VARIABLE_NUMBER` (32766 on 3.32+, 999 on older builds). The after-import cache refresh hit the same error, so the incremental baseline never persisted; every subsequent import fell back to a near-full Python scan in the in-process `WorkerThread`, holding the GIL and starving the web accept loop. Self-perpetuating. **Fix**: new `_fetch_books_in_chunks` helper splits the IN filter into 900-id batches (safe under the pre-3.32 999 floor) and concatenates the per-batch results; applied at both `Books.id.in_` sites in `find_duplicate_books_python` and `find_duplicate_books_sql`. Per-batch queries can only order within a batch, so each callsite re-sorts in Python using the tz-safe `_timestamp_or_default(b.timestamp, _AWARE_MIN)` key — Calibre libraries mix offset-naive and offset-aware `Books.timestamp` (DB `ORDER BY` tolerated it, Python's sort otherwise raised `can't compare offset-naive and offset-aware datetimes`). **9 new tests** across `tests/unit/test_duplicates_chunked_in.py` (chunk size below the 999 floor, empty-ids no-op, 170k-id full coverage, exact-multiple-of-chunk, set input accepted) and `tests/unit/test_duplicates_timezone.py` (mixed-tz total ordering without raise, source-pin that both callsites use the tz-safe key, source-pin that the raw `(b.timestamp is not None, b.timestamp)` crash pattern cannot return). RED on main, GREEN on this branch; 99/99 across every duplicate-touching unit-test file. **Live container verification on cwn-local with synthetic 170,231-id payload against real SQLite 3.50.4**: unchunked path raised `OperationalError: too many SQL variables` (exact production symptom); chunked path returned 3040 books in 0.58s, no error.
