| #247 | (fork issue [#234](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/234), reporter @thunderbolt93; inspired-by @navels in CWA [#1359](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/pull/1359)) | **Rendering the book grid during a concurrent ingest crashed with `AttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'id'` inside `cps.db.CalibreDB.order_authors`** — wire-symptom: 500 on `/` mid-ingest with `CWA_WATCH_MODE=poll`. **Root cause:** `order_authors()` re-queried `Authors` by `Books.author_sort` on every page render and assumed every result row plus every linked `book.authors` entry was a valid Authors object; a torn-down LEFT JOIN row (concurrent ingest/delete) could surface a `None` entry in the loaded collection, and the downstream `r.id` access blew up the whole page render. Two adjacent fragilities in the same function: `entry.author_sort.split('&')` raised when `author_sort` was NULL (Calibre allows it), and the `.first()` id-fallback could append None into `ordered_authors` and propagate into the template. **Fix:** consult the already-loaded `book.authors` collection instead of issuing fresh SQL during render — no render-time SQL means no session-state race window. None entries in `book.authors` are filtered before lookups; None / empty `author_sort` is treated as empty (no `.split` crash); stale sort entries log once per process via the existing fork-#108 `_AUTHOR_SORT_DRIFT_WARNED` rate-limit and fall through to id-fallback so every linked author still appears in the rendered order; last-resort safety net: if every sort entry is stale and no ids remain, return the linked authors so the book renders with its author list rather than appearing author-less. Structure adopted from CWA upstream PR #1359 (@navels) — same fix proposed upstream; this lands the relief in our build today rather than waiting for upstream review. Preserves our fork-original additions: the `_AUTHOR_SORT_DRIFT_WARNED` rate-limit (fork #108) and the linked-authors safety net. **8 new unit tests** in `tests/unit/test_order_authors_none_guard.py` cover the failure modes from the report (None author, None author_sort, stale sort, mixed linked entries, combined entry shape, id=None linked author, empty book.authors). RED on `main`, GREEN on this branch. | #279 | (CW issue [#3648](https://github.com/janeczku/calibre-web/issues/3648), reporter @NathanIfinity — reproduced in our build before fixing per the new "verify upstream issues against our divergent code" discipline) | **Amazon metadata search now returns results again** instead of "No Result(s) found! Please try another keyword!" for queries that obviously have matches. ComicVine and the Chinese provider returned results fine for the same query — the failure was Amazon-specific. **Root cause**: `cps/metadata_provider/amazon.py::Amazon.headers` declared only `User-Agent`, `Accept`, `Accept-Encoding`. | #291 | (revisits closed [#281](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/281); reproduced live during fork #276 work) | **`User.view_settings = NULL` no longer 500s the entire web UI for affected users.** `view_settings` is `Column(JSON, default={})`, but SQLAlchemy's `default=` only applies on INSERT through the ORM — rows imported from older schemas (pre-2025-01-14 when this column was added upstream) or inserted via raw SQL / external admin tools landed with NULL. Any affected user then hit `AttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'get'` at `cps/ub.py:235` in `User.get_view_property`. Because `layout.html`'s cover-settings cog calls `get_view_property` on every render, the affected user got a 500 on `/`, `/book/<id>`, `/table`, and every other page — effectively a per-user web UI lockout. **PR #281** proposed `vs = self.view_settings or {}` guards inside `get_view_property` / `set_view_property` and was closed on the wrong threshold ("no teenyverse production NULL rows"); I reproduced the exact crash later that day on cwn-local by manually setting `view_settings=NULL`. **Fix**: new `migrate_user_view_settings_null(engine, _session)` runs from the existing `migrate_Database` orchestrator between `migrate_user_table` and `migrate_shelf_table`. Single `UPDATE user SET view_settings = '{}' WHERE view_settings IS NULL`. Idempotent (zero rows match on re-run); no-op when no legacy NULLs exist; rowcount logged so operators can see whether any legacy NULLs were normalized. Also flips `Anonymous.__init__` initial value from `view_settings = None` to `view_settings = {}` for defense-in-depth — `loadSettings()` immediately overwrites it from the DB row, but with the migration that DB row is always `{}` so the Anonymous path can never bottom out at `None`. **6 source-pin tests** in `tests/unit/test_view_settings_null_migration.py` pin function definition, idempotent UPDATE shape (WHERE NULL filter + `'{}'` literal), rowcount log, orchestrator wiring, rollback-on-exception, Anonymous `__init__` uses `{}`. **Live end-to-end verified on cwn-local**: seeded `null-vs-test` with `view_settings=NULL`, restarted container → log shows `[view-settings-null-migration] normalized 1 user(s) with NULL view_settings to '{}'` → DB row now `{}` → user logs in successfully → `/` and `/book/5` render cleanly (pre-fix both 500'd with the AttributeError). | `bafd309a` | v4.0.116 |

| #309 | (production hotfix for #305 / v4.0.130) | **Annotation polymorphic migration uses PRAGMA instead of the stale SQLAlchemy inspector.** v4.0.130's `migrate_annotation_polymorphic_position` failed on the teenyverse deploy with `sqlite3.OperationalError: duplicate column name: position_type` even though the live `PRAGMA table_info(annotation)` showed the column absent — the `annotation` table shipped missing all 4 polymorphic columns (`position_type`, `pdf_page`, `pdf_quad_json`, `comic_page`), so the PDF + comic annotation overlays from #305 sub-projects 3+4 were inert on production. **Root cause**: SQLAlchemy's reflection cache (`inspect(engine)`) is stale after the preceding decouple migration's CREATE/DROP/RENAME sequence — `add_missing_tables` runs `Base.metadata.create_all` first (creating an `annotation` placeholder with the full current model schema, polymorphic columns included), then the decouple migration drops that placeholder + renames `kobo_annotation_sync` → `annotation` (H1-era columns only); the cached inspector kept returning the placeholder's column set, so the existence guard diverged from the real post-rename table + the `ADD COLUMN` fired against a mismatched view. **Fix**: query the live SQLite catalog via `PRAGMA table_info(annotation)` INSIDE the same transaction that runs the `ADD COLUMN`, so the existence check + DDL see the identical DB view; plus per-statement `try/except` catching `duplicate column` as belt-and-suspenders idempotency (one already-present column no longer aborts the rest). **4 regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_annotation_polymorphic_stale_inspector.py` reproduce the exact teenyverse failure (table already has `position_type`), happy path (bare table → all 4), full-noop, and no-table cases. 292 annotation/kobo/hardcover tests green. No data at risk — nullable `ADD COLUMN`s, teenyverse had 0 annotation rows. **Live verified on teenyverse**: `[annotation-polymorphic-position] added 4 columns` in logs, all 4 columns present in the live schema. | `9ad240b2` | v4.0.131 |
| #310 | (fork issue [#288](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/288) — two mobile bugs caught on a real iPhone) | **Book titles no longer overlap covers + pagination arrow vertically aligned on mobile.** Two bugs the operator caught on a real iPhone that did NOT reproduce on localhost (Chromium or headless WebKit) — the sim-vs-device split was the diagnostic clue. **Bug 1 (titles overlap covers)**: the home grid uses isotope masonry (`main.js`, `layoutMode: fitRowsCentered`) which absolutely-positions each `.book` card from its measured height at document-ready. On a cold mobile-Safari load the Open Sans web font arrives AFTER isotope lays out, so cards are measured with fallback-font metrics; when the real font swaps in, multi-line titles reflow taller but the absolute positions are stale → titles overlap the covers above. There was no relayout on `document.fonts.ready` and phones never fire `window.resize`, so it never self-corrected (localhost serves the font instantly, hiding the race). **Fix**: (a) `main.js` relayouts the discover isotope grid on `document.fonts.ready` + `window load` (guarded for browsers without the Font Loading API); (b) `fork-mobile-cards.css` reserves a deterministic 2-line title height (`min-height: 2.5em`) so every card is a CONSTANT height regardless of title length or font-load timing — isotope can't mis-measure, making overlap structurally impossible even if a relayout is missed. Proven in actual WebKit with the font response delayed 4s (forcing the fallback-metrics layout): 0 overlaps + uniform 285px card heights both during the delay and after the font + relayout settle. **Bug 2 (pagination arrow misaligned)**: caliBlur sizes the prev/next arrow `<a>` + `:before` glyph with desktop dimensions (`line-height: 60px; padding: 20px 25px; height: 60px`) tuned for its 60px-tall desktop pagination bar; against ~33px mobile page buttons the arrow centered ~9px low. **Fix**: mobile flex-row pagination (`align-items: center`) + collapse the arrow box (`line-height: 1; height: auto; padding: 0 10px; margin-right: 0`) to match the button height — arrow center now 69px == page-button center 69px (was 78 vs 69). **7 regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_mobile_isotope_overlap_and_arrow.py`; 12/12 mobile-layout tests green. Desktop verified unchanged at 1280px (pagination block/fixed, title nowrap/no-min-height — all scoped to `@media max-width: 767px`). | `3c5f3b8f` | v4.0.132 |
| #313 | (real-device fix for #305 sub-project 2 — live Kobo annotation capture) | **Kobo annotation capture now actually routes to CWNG when Kobo sync is on, independent of Hardcover.** Caught by a real-device test (Maggie's Kobo, 2026-05-24): the device synced, CWNG received library-sync requests + the self-signed cert was trusted, but CWNG captured 0 annotations — no annotation PATCH reached CWNG at all. **Root cause**: Kobo annotations sync to the *reading-services* host (`readingservices.kobo.com`), a different host than the library/store API. CWNG's `/v1/initialization` response (`cps/kobo.py HandleInitRequest`) rewrites `reading_services_host` to point at CWNG so the device sends annotations to us — but both branches (proxied + unproxied) gated that rewrite on `config.config_hardcover_annotations_sync and bool(hardcover)`. #305 sub-project (2) decoupled the annotation *capture handler* (`cps/readingservices.py handle_annotations`) from Hardcover, but missed this *routing* gate in the init handshake. With Hardcover off (the default), the Init response left `reading_services_host` at `readingservices.kobo.com`, so the device sent annotations straight to Kobo's cloud and CWNG's capture handler was never reached — live Kobo capture was a no-op on the wire. **Fix**: gate the redirect on `config.config_kobo_sync` (the master Kobo sync toggle) in both branches. Safe because `proxy_to_kobo_reading_services()` unconditionally forwards every reading-services request on to Kobo's real servers — CWNG is a passive tap: reading state + annotations still reach Kobo's cloud, CWNG just also captures a local copy. **2 regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_kobo_init_library_sync_rewrite.py` pin that both branches gate `reading_services_host` on `config_kobo_sync` + the solely-Hardcover guard is gone; 283 kobo+annotation tests green. **Why it shipped despite #305's 288 tests + claimed 5-angle e2e**: every non-device test exercised the capture handler directly (synthetic PATCH); none verified the init handshake that decides whether a real device routes there. This is the class of bug only a real-device test catches — final confirmation is the device re-test on this release. | `d66b3d02` | v4.0.133 |
| #314 | (web-reader overlay fix for #305 sub-project 5 — follow-on from the #313 real-device test) | **Captured Kobo highlights now resolve a CFI and render as overlays in the in-browser reader, including live-captured ones with NULL child_index.** After #313 made live Kobo capture route to CWNG, the captured highlights still didn't render as colored overlays in the web reader. **Root cause**: `cps/services/kobo_position.py compute_cfi_range` only used the KoboSpan *selector* path when `start/end_container_child_index == -99` (`KOBO_SELECTOR_SENTINEL` — the value Kobo writes in `KoboReader.sqlite`). But the live reading-services PATCH omits `StartContainerChildIndex` entirely, so live-captured kepub annotations store it as **NULL**. With NULL: selector path skipped → child-index path returned None (no index) → highlight resolved to no CFI → the web reader had nothing to anchor an overlay to. Affected every live-captured Kobo highlight. **Fix**: take the selector path whenever both KoboSpan IDs are present (`start_id and end_id`), independent of `child_index`. The span IDs are the reliable kepub anchor; the child-index DOM walk remains for plain EPUBs with no span IDs (unchanged, still gated by absence of IDs). The `-99` sentinel case is now a subset of 'IDs present', preserving existing behavior. **Verified against the real Nineteen Eighty-Four kepub** (book 523 on the production library): all four of Maggie's annotations — her 2 real Kobo highlights (NULL child_index) + 2 test annotations — now resolve to valid `epubcfi()` strings (e.g. `epubcfi(/6/8!/4[kobo.0.15]:0,/4[kobo.0.15]:56)` for the 'BIG BROTHER IS WATCHING YOU' line). The `/annotations/<book>/data.json` endpoint computes + persists `cfi_range` on first read (via `_ensure_cfi_range`), so existing annotations heal on next load with no data migration. The `/annotations/<book>` view page + Markdown/CSV/JSON exports were separately verified to render all annotations (text, note, color) against the real prod data. **New regression test** `test_live_capture_null_child_index_uses_selector` pins the NULL-child-index selector path; existing `-99` sentinel tests unchanged (now a subset); 284 kobo+annotation tests green. CI hit the xdist worker-IPC hang twice, green on 2nd rerun. | `b29a41a0` | v4.0.134 |
| #317 | (web-reader overlay **render** fix for #305 — follow-on from #314) | **Captured Kobo highlights now actually paint as colored overlays in the web reader.** v4.0.134 made the converter return a CFI, but the highlights still never drew on the page — the sidebar listed them, the page stayed blank. **Root cause (two bugs).** (1) The CFI the server computed was unresolvable by epub.js: `epubcfi(/6/8!/4[kobo.0.15]:0,…)` asserts the KoboSpan *is* the document body (`/4`) with a character offset attached directly to an element step. epub.js resolves highlight CFIs via a position-constrained XPath (`stepsToXpath` → `./*/*[position()=2 and @id='kobo.0.15']`) against its rendered DOM, where the span is actually nested several levels deep (`/4/2[book-columns]/2[book-inner]/…`), so it returned `No startContainer found` and drew nothing. (2) `annotations.js` built the highlight class as `"cwa-annotation-overlay cwa-annotation-overlay-" + color`; real Kobo devices store a hex color (`#F6F3B3`, not `"yellow"`), so `classList.add()` threw `InvalidCharacterError` on the space + `#`. **Fix (root cause): a highlight CFI is reader-specific — only the reader can produce one it can resolve.** The KoboSpan id is the one anchor stable across rendering, so the reader now resolves the span in the live document via `getElementById`, builds a DOM Range from the stored offsets (TreeWalker handles nested inline markup), and calls epub.js's own `contents.cfiFromRange(range)` to generate the canonical CFI before highlighting — applied per section on the `rendered` event so it survives navigation. `data.json` now carries the KoboSpan anchors (`start_kobospan`/`end_kobospan` + offsets + `content_id`); colors map (named **or** hex) to an rgba fill + a sanitized class token. `read_book` serves the KEPUB to authenticated users with annotations on an EPUB-family book (the spans only exist in the kepub), with the reading position falling back across the epub/kepub pair so it isn't orphaned. The server-side converter (export/portability) now walks the chapter DOM to emit a structurally valid 3-part source CFI (offsets on text nodes) instead of the invalid element-offset form, and prefers the KEPUB when locating the file on disk. **Why #314's verification missed it**: #314 confirmed the converter *returned* a CFI string + that `data.json` served it; it never drove epub.js to actually resolve+paint that CFI in a browser. This fix was found and verified with Playwright against a live reader. **Verified live**: all four test highlights (two hex `#F6F3B3`, two named `red`; single-span + cross-paragraph) render with exact text coverage (3/3 single-span text matches; cross-span covers precisely its anchor extent), survive paging away and back, position correctly on a 390px mobile viewport and in dark mode, console clean of both prior errors. **Tests**: converter assertions updated to the valid CFI form + a round-trip test that walks the generated CFI back to the highlighted text; `_data_json_row` contract test pins the KoboSpan anchor fields + hex-color pass-through; 89 kobo+annotation tests green. | `2c79bc4` | v4.0.135 |
| #285 | (fork issue [#283](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/283), reporter @droM4X) | **Three UI bugs in the Books List (`/table`) bulk-editor's Comments dialog.** (1) Saved or newly typed text rendered as **light gray on white** — almost invisible. | #335 | (fork issues [#326](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/326) audit by @jbelascoain + [#308](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/308) reporter @Glennza1962 + [#331](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/331) reporter @Gusdezup) | **Kobo sync no longer silently fails behind nginx + admin spinner constrained at the CSS layer.** Two independent fork-side reports converge on the same root cause: nginx's default `proxy_buffer_size` (4 KB) and `proxy_buffers` (8 × 4 KB) are too small for CWA's `/v1/library/sync` response headers (auth, sync tokens, library state). nginx silently drops the response. The CWA log shows no error; the Kobo shows *"Sync failed, please try again."* Both reporters independently traced it to bumping the buffer directives. **Fix**: README gets a "nginx buffer sizes (important for Kobo sync)" callout in the Kobo sync section with the three load-bearing directives (`proxy_buffer_size 32k; proxy_buffers 4 32k; proxy_busy_buffers_size 64k;`), Synology DSM + Nginx Proxy Manager-specific notes, and a link to a new `examples/nginx-reverse-proxy.conf` reference snippet. Troubleshooting entry for *"Sync failed, please try again"* adds buffer-cause as a numbered item so symptom-searchers land here. **Bundled #326 audit by @jbelascoain** — community PR proposed swapping the loading spinner gif to a nicer-looking 250×250 version, but the five `<img id="img-spinner">` callsites (admin Restart/Status modals + config_db + config_edit + cwa_settings) carry no width/height attrs, so the new gif would have rendered at full native size everywhere. Constrain the rendered size at the CSS layer (`#img-spinner, #img-spinner2 { width: 48px; height: 48px; box-shadow: none; }`) so a future gif swap can't regress, and centralise the box-shadow cleanup @jbelascoain inlined in admin.html. **13 source-pinning regression tests** across `tests/unit/test_331_308_nginx_buffer_docs.py` (12) + `tests/unit/test_326_spinner_sizing.py` (3): README mentions both proxy directives + explicitly warns about the silent-failure mode (the #1 diagnostic mistake), troubleshooting entry includes buffer cause, README links to reference config, reference config exists with ≥32K floor + X-Forwarded-* headers + Kobo-buffer motivation comment + modern `http2 on;` directive (not the deprecated `listen ... http2;` combined form), CSS rule exists with ≤96px width/height + box-shadow:none, every template referencing loading-icon.gif uses the constrained id. **Greptile 5/5** after one round of revisions (caught the deprecated http2 syntax + technically-wrong "inherited" wording in the CSS comment — both addressed). | `fb4134a3` | v4.0.139 |

| #333 | (fork issue [#318](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/318), reporter @thealmostmighty) | **Manual duplicate-scan + auto-resolve buttons no longer refused on stale follow-up marker.** Both endpoints in `cps/duplicates.py` (`trigger_scan` for the *Run Full Scan* button and `execute_resolution` for the *Execute Auto-Resolution* button) gated on `ingest_batch_follow_up_pending()`, which returns True if any of `cwa_ingest_batch_active`, `cwa_ingest_batch_dirty`, or `cwa_ingest_batch_dirty.running` marker files exist. The dirty/running markers signal "s6 post-batch follow-up hasn't run yet" — NOT "ingest is currently writing books". A stale dirty marker can persist after a clean ingest finishes or after an abnormal container shutdown, **permanently blocking the user's button until the marker is removed by hand**. The task-level gate in `cps/tasks/duplicate_scan.py` is the single source of truth: full scan + non-manual trigger + ingest-pending → skip; manual triggers are exempt by design. The endpoint-level gates shared the same condition but missed the manual carve-out. Fix: remove the redundant endpoint-level gates from both routes. **10 regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_duplicate_trigger_scan_not_gated_by_pending_followup.py` source-pin (a) both endpoints no longer reference the followup-pending check, (b) both endpoints no longer emit the `ingest_in_progress` blocked response, (c) `trigger_scan` still queues `TaskDuplicateScan` with `trigger_type='manual'`, (d) task-level gate is preserved (still calls the check, still exempts manual triggers). | #337 | (fork issue [#319](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/319), reporters @SethMilliken + @droM4X) | **Per-user hide: recoverability bug-class closed AND user-hostility UX causes addressed.** Two halves shipped together. **Bug-half (droM4X verification):** clicking the metadata icon, reading icon, or download icon on a user's own hidden book all bounced with "Selected book is unavailable"; covers were missing from `/hidden/stored` and the detail page; the `/hidden` URL had no discovery surface. Root cause: `get_filtered_book` is the helper every action route uses; v4.0.136 only extended `get_book_read_archived`. Fix: extend `CalibreDB.get_filtered_book` with `allow_show_hidden=False` kwarg (mirroring `allow_show_archived`, default False — every existing caller's semantics unchanged), thread `True` from the eight detail-page action callsites a user can reach for their own hidden book (`get_book_cover` + `get_download_link` in `helper.py`; `serve_book` + `read_book` + audio-reader inner lookup in `web.py`; `render_edit_book` + `do_edit_book` + `get_sorted_entry` in `editbooks.py`). Discoverability: `/me` profile gets a "Hidden Books (N)" button, gated on `hidden_book_count > 0`. **UX-safety half (SethMilliken's original report):** the hide feature shipped on-by-default with the same eye icon as Read/Unread (adjacent buttons), so it was easy to accidentally hide. Three fixes: (1) new `config_user_hide_enabled = Column(Boolean, default=False)` on `_Settings` (idempotent ALTER via `_migrate_table` reflection — legacy DBs gain the column on first boot post-upgrade), admin toggles it in Feature Configuration; the hide button is now suppressed until admin opts in. (2) Read-status icon swapped from `glyphicon-eye-open` / `glyphicon-eye-close` to `glyphicon-ok` / `glyphicon-unchecked` (droM4X's exact wording: "should be changed to a checkmark"); hide button keeps the eye, eliminating the visual collision. (3) Hide button moved to the END of the action row (after Delete) — now 232px from the read-status button on rendered pages. **Defense-in-depth recovery** (admins must not be able to strand users' already-hidden books): `/ajax/togglehidden/<id>` always allows unhide of an existing row but refuses new hides (HTTP 403 + INFO log) when the flag is off; detail-page hide button gate is `(g.user_hide_enabled or is_hidden)` so unhide stays available; `/me` Hidden Books link is count-gated, not flag-gated. `g.user_hide_enabled` is populated in `admin.py`'s `@admi.before_app_request` (mirroring `g.allow_anonymous`) because Jinja's `config` global is Flask's `app.config`, not `cps.config` (PR #335 lesson). **38 source-pin regression tests** in `tests/unit/test_user_hidden_books.py` + new `test_user_hide_ux_safety_319.py` — RED on the v4.0.139 baseline, GREEN with this fix; full unit suite 1203 passing. **Hungarian + German translations** for the two new admin-form strings; all 28 .mo files recompile per `tests/unit/test_translations_compile.py`. **Live `cwn-local` end-to-end with Playwright + direct HTTP**: default-off (no hide button), admin toggle persists (`Felhasználók elrejthetik a könyveket a saját könyvtárukból`), hide click → DB row + icon flip + `/me` shows "HIDDEN BOOKS (1)" + `/hidden/stored` shows cover + all action icons work on the hidden book; admin disables flag → already-hidden book detail page: unhide button still renders and works; direct POST bypass with flag off → HTTP 403 + log line. **Greptile P2 catch addressed**: the `change_profile()` validation-error re-render now also passes `hidden_book_count`, so the recovery link doesn't silently disappear after a bad save. Out of scope per "implement what's asked" rule: confirmation modal on hide-click (no reporter requested), admin-vs-user-level hide split (droM4X's architectural proposal, not a fix-this ask), auto-shelf for hidden books (SethMilliken's alternative to docs — `/me` link satisfies the discoverability ask). | `a5200d21` | v4.0.140 |

| #371 | [fork #370](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/370) (community report + patch by @8bitgentleman) | **`POST /duplicates/invalidate-cache` requires authentication.** The endpoint had `@csrf.exempt` but no auth decorators — unauthenticated clients (including the public internet on exposed installs) could force duplicate-cache invalidations (low-grade DoS; least-privilege violation). Copy-paste omission: the adjacent `trigger-scan` route already carried `@login_required_if_no_ano` + `@admin_or_edit_required`. Merged the contributor's 2-line fix + structural regression tests as-is under the `community-contribution` validate-author exemption (authorship preserved). Independent cross-check before merge: the ingest service no longer calls this endpoint (`scripts/ingest_processor.py` uses `/cwa-internal/*` since the #1353-era rework), so adding auth breaks no internal caller. First community security contribution to the fork. | `3d8628627` | v4.0.156 |

| #201 | inspired by [janeczku/calibre-web#3625](https://github.com/janeczku/calibre-web/pull/3625) (@jvoisin) | XSS hardening on book-comment render path. Janeczku's PR #3625 routed only the custom-column `comments`-type `column.value\|safe` render through `clean_string`. | #197 | (closes the route-collision behind #196 from @droM4X) **Docker HEALTHCHECK probed the wrong endpoint.** `Dockerfile:311` ran `curl -fsL http://localhost:${CWA_PORT_OVERRIDE:-8083}/` which redirects to `/login` and returns 200 regardless of whether the Calibre `metadata.db` is reachable. | #178 | (fork issue [#160](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/160), reporter @droM4X) | **OPDS locale resolver chain for anonymous clients.** Continuation of #121 ([#137](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/137) + [#138](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/138)) — those landed the `N_()` wrappers + the Hungarian translations, but droM4X's follow-up reported that clients sending no `Accept-Language` (Readest, KOReader, some Kobo clients) still got English because the Guest user has `locale='en'`. | #186 | (fork issue [#160](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/160) follow-up, reporter @droM4X) | **OPDS `?lang=` propagation through navigation/pagination/search/OSD.** Continuation of #178 / v4.0.56 — that PR shipped the four-step locale resolver in `cps/cw_babel.py:get_locale()`, but every link in the OPDS XML response was built with bare `url_for(...)` and dropped `?lang=hu` on the floor. Set `?lang=hu` on `/opds`, get Hungarian root, click any nav entry, revert to English. @droM4X's "only the second half of the task was implemented" caught this — the resolver was in, the response side of the loop wasn't. Four parts: (1) new `@opds.url_defaults` callback injects `lang` from `request.args` into every `url_for` in the OPDS blueprint when not already set, so following any nav link preserves the language; (2) pagination `rel=first|next|previous` links now use new `_opds_paged_url` helper that preserves every inbound query arg except `offset` — was: `request.path + '?offset=N'` which clobbered everything; (3) `/opds/search/<path:query>` strips the URL query string from `RAW_URI` before splitting out the search term — without this, `url_defaults` adding `?lang=hu` to every search URL made `.split('/opds/search/')[1]` capture `term?lang=hu` as the search term, and every path-form search would have returned zero matches; (4) `/opds/osd` advertises the resolved request locale via `get_locale()` instead of hardcoded `en-EN`, and its OpenSearch URL templates compose `{searchTerms}` correctly relative to any propagated query string (path-form keeps the marker in the URL path; query-form joins with `&` when a query string is already present). 16 regression tests in `tests/unit/test_opds_lang_propagation_160.py` source-pin every fix (so a refactor can't silently regress) and behaviorally drive Flask `url_for` and `_opds_paged_url` under varied request contexts. **Live-verified on cwn-local against a 21-book library**: `/opds?lang=hu` titles Hungarian + all nav hrefs carry `?lang=hu`; `/opds/new?lang=hu&offset=5` has `rel=next` = `…&offset=10` and `rel=first` strips offset; pagination tooltip = "Következő" (Hungarian for "Next"); `/opds/search/crime?lang=hu` returns 1 match identical to no-lang variant (search term not contaminated); `/opds/osd?lang=de` advertises `<Language>de</Language>` with clean URL templates; mixed 60 concurrent requests (30 anon + 30 admin) all 200, zero errors in container logs; malformed `lang=` values (empty, garbage, SQLi-shaped, `<script>`) → 200 with en fallback, no 500s; locale normalization `pt-BR` ≡ `pt_BR` ≡ pt_BR translation, `zh-Hans-CN` → Chinese Simplified; 4-quadrant auth matrix unchanged from PR #137/#178; #121 regression check shows 0 WARN log lines for anonymous probes. | `d04be560` | v4.0.57 |
| #161 | Community contribution from @Amjad50 — **drag-and-drop book merge with per-format conflict resolution**. Drag one book cover onto another in the grid to merge their formats; the source book is deleted after merge, the keeper retains all formats. When the source and keeper share a format, a confirmation modal surfaces a per-format radio (Keep existing / Replace with source). Server-side: existing `/ajax/mergebooks` endpoint extended with optional `overwrite_formats` list (backwards-compatible — empty list = original keep-only behavior); `@user_login_required` + `@edit_required` decorators block anonymous and view-only users (verified: viewer-role curl POST → 403). Client-side: CSS / modal HTML / JS bundle gated behind `{% if current_user.is_authenticated and current_user.role_edit() %}` so read-only users never receive the surface. CSRF via global Flask-WTF middleware + `X-CSRFToken` header. JS adds drag-flicker prevention via shield divs, focus on Cancel by default, multiple close affordances (Cancel button / Esc / backdrop click), MutationObserver for dynamically-loaded books, no-op-during-multi-select-mode gating. Live-verified end-to-end on cwn-local with Playwright: single-conflict modal (book 3 → 6) shows 1 EPUB conflict row + EPUB+PDF result preview; two-conflict modal (book 7 → 6) shows both EPUB + PDF rows; replace-then-confirm flow merges correctly with source deletion + file replacement on disk. PR landed under the operator-applied `community-contribution` label which exempts validate-author. Credit @Amjad50 (Amjad Alsharafi). | `550595c5` | v4.0.56 |
| #156 | **Deflake `test_cwa_db` + `test_generate_checksums`** (the two long-documented "pre-existing CI flakes" finally root-caused and fixed). Two deterministic bugs that have failed intermittently for months depending on CI worker load + test ordering. **Root cause #1**: `scripts/cwa_db.py:22` hardcoded `self.db_path = "/config/"` regardless of the `CWA_DB_PATH` env var the test fixture (`tests/conftest.py:331`) was already setting via `monkeypatch.setenv`. Every parallel pytest-xdist worker opened the same shared `/config/cwa.db`, surfacing as `sqlite3.OperationalError: database is locked` under write contention and wrong-timestamp readbacks where one worker's INSERT for `book_id=1` overwrote another's. Fix reads `CWA_DB_PATH` (defaults to `/config/` so production is byte-identical) and `os.makedirs(..., exist_ok=True)` before sqlite3 connect for defense-in-depth (also unblocks the pre-existing buggy `test_handles_missing_database_gracefully` that pointed at a non-existent tmp_path subdir expecting auto-creation). **Root cause #2**: `scripts/generate_book_checksums.py:36-37` imported `cps.progress_syncing.checksums` + `cps.progress_syncing.settings` at module top, forcing a full `cps/__init__.py` boot (Flask + SQLAlchemy + plugins + logger) on every subprocess invocation. Measured ~1.5s locally; 30+s under CI parallel-worker contention, tripping the 30s `subprocess.run(..., timeout=30)` in the test. Fix moves the heavy imports inside `generate_checksums()` body and adds a `_check_koreader_sync_enabled_lightweight()` helper that reads the `cwa_settings.koreader_sync_enabled` column via direct sqlite3 (honoring `CWA_DB_PATH`, fail-closed semantics matching production) so the early-exit path doesn't pay any cps cost. Disabled-path subprocess: 1.5s+ → **0.039s**. Test timeouts also bumped 30s→120s with explanatory comment as belt-and-suspenders against future regression. 3 new regression tests pin: env-var-respect, `/config/` default-when-unset, parallel-instance-with-distinct-paths isolation. **Verified**: CI passed cleanly on first run (Fast Tests + Test Suite Summary green, no `--admin` override). After this PR, future PRs ship through CI without flake-driven retries — the `--admin` override used to merge #149 (Phase 2 cover-preview) is no longer necessary for the documented "pre-existing flakes" reason. | `80b7bc7c` | v4.0.52 |
| #208 | **Move single-instance lock acquisition out of module-import time** in the three scheduled scripts (`scripts/ingest_processor.py`, `scripts/kindle_epub_fixer.py`, `scripts/convert_library.py`). All three historically did `open(path, 'x')` + `atexit.register(removeLock)` + `sys.exit(2)` on collision **at the module top level** — which meant `importlib.import_module(...)` from a pytest-xdist worker (workers share `/tmp` across processes) could crash a sibling worker that had already taken the same lock. That's the root cause behind the test-isolation flake patched narrowly by #204 (test-only mitigation, deeper refactor deferred). Each script now has a `_acquire_lock_or_exit()` (or `_acquire_process_lock_or_exit()`) helper called from `main()` — importing the module is a pure load with no filesystem side-effects. `convert_library.py` also hardened for CI / non-container environments (missing `/config` dir, missing `abc` user) with `try/except` around its `FileHandler` setup and the `pwd.getpwnam('abc')` lookup, so a test runner can subprocess-import the script without root and without the LinuxServer image's user table. New regression test `tests/unit/test_script_import_side_effects.py` (20 tests) pins the contract via three layers: (1) subprocess imports of each script return rc=0 and create no lockfile in `/tmp`, both with no prior lockfile and with a stale sibling-script lockfile present; (2) AST source-pin tests assert no module-level `sys.exit()` on lock collision and no module-level `atexit.register()` — a future refactor that re-introduces import-time side effects fails the test; (3) AST wire-up test asserts each script's `main()` actually calls its `_acquire_lock_or_exit()` helper, so a refactor that silently removes the call (losing single-instance protection in production while the import-side-effect tests still pass) is caught. Verified locally: all 20 tests green, `python3 -c 'import <script>'` for each creates no lockfile in `/tmp`. Eliminates the entire class of "PR landed red Fast Tests because of cross-xdist-worker lockfile pollution" that #204 patched narrowly. | `b141b672` | v4.0.64 |
| #209 | Community contribution from @RichardGubijev — **"Apply Default Settings" admin button is now red (`btn-danger`) to differentiate it visually from the adjacent grey "Submit" button.** Reporter's rationale: they'd hit the destructive button by accident multiple times while looking for "Submit" next to it. | #246 | (fork issue [#244](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/244)) **Integration test suite `test_ingest_checksums.py` was failing on every PR opened against `main` since v4.0.79 / PR #238 shipped** — six tests assertion-failed with `len(checksums) == 0`. After 6 consecutive autopilot ticks blocked at the repo-WIP precondition gate, this lands the proper fix. **Root cause:** PR #238 / fork #219 gated `book_format_checksums` writes on `cwa_settings.koreader_sync_enabled` so disabled-sync instances skip the slow partial-MD5 work. The schema default in `scripts/cwa_schema.sql` is 0, so a fresh test container left the suite asserting against zero rows. **Fix:** module-scoped autouse fixture flips the flag to 1 on the session container before any test in the module runs, then resets it to 0 on teardown so the session-scoped container is clean for later modules. `is_koreader_sync_enabled()` in `cps/progress_syncing/settings.py` re-reads `cwa_settings` via a fresh `CWA_DB()` on every call, so the in-container ingest_processor picks up the flip without a service restart. **Rejected alternative:** the WIP version of this branch added `pytest.skip()` when the flag was 0 — that would have made CI green but stopped exercising the actual ingest -> checksum-write path. Coverage theater, not a fix. CI green on the fix: Integration Tests (Docker) passed cleanly on the first run. | `706fd74d` | v4.0.85 |
| #282 | (diagnostic follow-up to `notes/pr-281-ci-hang-diagnosis-2026-05-21.md`) **CI fast-tests now surfaces hung tests as named failures instead of opaque step timeouts.** PR #281's Fast Tests job timed out after 10 minutes with no indication of which test or which pytest-xdist worker hung — visible stdout ended at `[gw0] [97%]` then 9 minutes of silence. Same opacity blocked PRs #279, #280, #266. Root cause for the opacity (separate from the underlying flake): `pytest -n auto` parallelism with no per-test timeout means a stuck test on one worker only manifests as a step-level 10-minute timeout, with no signal pointing to which test or worker stalled. Adds `--timeout=120 --timeout-method=thread` to the pytest invocation in `.github/workflows/tests.yml`. Future hangs surface as named test failures with stack traces. `thread` method is required because pytest-xdist parallel mode breaks the default `signal`-based timeout. `pytest-timeout>=2.2.0` is already installed via `requirements-dev.txt` — no dependency change. Step-level `timeout-minutes: 10` retained as last-resort kill. No app behavior change. | `7a66b060` | v4.0.110 |
| #296 | (CI flake mitigation, follow-up to PR #282 + notes/xdist-worker-ipc-hang-followup-2026-05-21.md) | **Two CI workflow mitigations for the xdist worker-IPC hang flake.** PR after PR through v4.0.110–v4.0.121 hit a documented xdist worker-IPC hang on ~1/3 of Test Suite runs: pytest-xdist's master waits forever for a worker between assignments, no currently-executing test for `pytest-timeout` to interrupt, only the step-level 10-minute kill catches it. Two complementary changes in `.github/workflows/tests.yml`: **(1) Scope `push.branches`** from `['**']` to `[main, dev]`. Previously a fork-branch push fired BOTH the `push` event AND the `pull_request` event for the same SHA → two parallel Test Suite runs competing for the same xdist resources, doubling the hang surface. Now PR branches get CI exclusively via `pull_request:`. Verified self-applying on PR #296's own CI: only 1 Test Suite run triggered on push (was 2 previously). Cuts CI minutes by ~50% too. **(2) Add `--dist=loadfile`** to the Fast Tests pytest invocation. Default xdist `--dist=loadbalance` work-steals individual tests between workers — the work-stealing race is exactly the failure mode the prior investigation fingered. `loadfile` pins each test file to a single worker → fewer handoffs → fewer races. Keeps `-n auto` so parallelism remains. **3 source-pin tests** in `tests/unit/test_ci_xdist_hang_mitigation.py` prevent silent regression: push.branches doesn't include `'**'`, pytest invocation includes `--dist=loadfile`, `--timeout=120 --timeout-method=thread` (PR #282) still present. **Empirical**: PR #296's own CI failed once at the same 10-min step timeout on the same `test_store_checksum_after_ensure_calibre_db_tables` test, then went green on rerun. So `--dist=loadfile` reduces but doesn't eliminate the hang — there's a residual issue (possibly a sqlite C-level mutex that `--timeout-method=thread` can't interrupt). Residual hang tracked in the same followup note for v2. The push-trigger fix alone is unambiguous progress: halves CI surface regardless of whether the test-specific bug ever gets diagnosed. | `2f2ecdc9` | v4.0.122 |
| #297 | (root-causes the residual half of the xdist worker-IPC hang flake — followup to #296 / v4.0.122) | **Sqlite connection cleanup in `test_store_checksum_after_ensure_calibre_db_tables`** — root cause of the residual xdist hang traced and eliminated. PR #296 (v4.0.122) added two surface-area mitigations (push-trigger scope + `--dist=loadfile`) but one of #296's own CI runs still timed out at exactly the same `test_store_checksum_after_ensure_calibre_db_tables` step. **Root cause**: the test called `conn = sqlite3.connect(str(db_path))` but never `conn.close()`. When the test function returned, the connection became unreachable → gc'd → `__del__` ran `sqlite3_close` at the C level — which can block on the sqlite mutex. Under pytest-xdist this gc happens DURING the worker → master IPC handoff: if sqlite's `__del__` blocks waiting on a mutex while xdist is also waiting for the worker's 'finished' signal, the master deadlocks. The test's assertions all pass but the runner never receives the completion signal — master waits the full 9 minutes until the step-level 10-minute kill fires. **Fix**: wrap the test body in `try/finally` with explicit `conn.close()`. Connection closes synchronously at the end of the test, before the worker hands the result back to the master. sqlite mutex released before IPC. Pure test-hygiene change — no production code change. **Empirical confirmation**: PR #297's CI passed first try, single run, no rerun-on-flake. After v4.0.110–v4.0.122 needed reruns on roughly half of all PR submissions due to this hang, the first PR after the fix sailed through cleanly. Addresses `notes/xdist-worker-ipc-hang-followup-2026-05-21.md` from the original investigation. | `a005762e` | v4.0.123 |
| #300 | (final xdist hang fix — closes the four-PR series; follow-up to PRs #296 / #297 / #298) | **Reclassified the cps-import-triggering test as integration so it no longer runs in the Fast Tests xdist pool.** PR #297 closed an unhandled sqlite connection and PR #298 deferred a heavy `cps` import inside `store_checksum`, both reducing the xdist worker-IPC hang incidence but not eliminating it. Tracing the next-shallowest source: the test does `from cps.progress_syncing.models import ensure_calibre_db_tables`, and `cps/progress_syncing/models.py` imports `cps.db` (full SQLAlchemy Base + heavy calibre-library wiring) and `cps.ub` (user database with all migrations) at module level. Both trigger the heavyweight cps package init — under pytest-xdist subprocess context those imports hang on resources that don't exist in the worker. Refactoring the module-level imports would require touching modules used throughout cps (out of scope for a CI flake fix). The test isn't a unit test by definition: it does real sqlite I/O AND triggers heavyweight cps init. **Fix**: change the class decorator from `@pytest.mark.unit` to `@pytest.mark.integration`. Moves the test out of the Fast Tests xdist pool entirely — Integration Tests runs in a separate CI job under Docker without the same parallelism issues. PR #300's own CI passed first try, no rerun needed — first datapoint of a clean run since the hang started cropping up across v4.0.110+. **Four-PR series summary**: #296 (drop dual-trigger CI surface + `--dist=loadfile`) → #297 (close sqlite connection in `try/finally`) → #298 (defer cps import inside `store_checksum`) → #300 (move test to integration). Each PR reduced the hang surface; #300 eliminates it from Fast Tests entirely. Addresses `notes/xdist-worker-ipc-hang-followup-2026-05-21.md`. **Coincidentally GitHub PR #300** — fork milestone. | `6e5184eb` | v4.0.126 |
| #321 | CI: `validate-author` skips merge commits (`--no-merges`) so a web-UI "Update branch" doesn't block auto-merge. The committer scan flagged any commit whose committer email wasn't new-usemame's; GitHub's "Update branch" button produces a merge commit committed by `GitHub <noreply@github.com>` (the clicker is the author, not the committer), so every PR that sat long enough for `main` to advance and need a branch update failed the gate — a recurring catch-22 unrelated to who authored the code (observed blocking docs PR #316 after a 14:03Z web-UI update). Merge commits carry no original authored content; their parents are validated independently. Substantive single-parent commits by a foreign committer are still caught (no over-relaxation). Wall 7 in `tests/unit/test_workflow_safety_invariants.py` (3 tests) source-pins `--no-merges` and behaviorally verifies a web-UI merge commit is skipped while a foreign non-merge commit is still flagged. | `e5597943` | v4.0.136 |

| #106 | Fork issue [#103](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/103) / mirrors janeczku [#3274](https://github.com/janeczku/calibre-web/issues/3274). `do_download_file()` did `download_name + "." + book_format` in five places without validating that `data.name` (which becomes `book_name` and propagates into `download_name` in three of the four code branches) or `book_format` is a usable string. A calibre.db `data` row with NULL `name`, or a caller with `book_format=None`, fell into `None + "."` deep inside the function and raised an unhandled `TypeError` — Flask surfaced it as a 500. Fix adds a precondition guard at the top of the function that aborts(400) with a diagnostic log line naming the offending book id + format. Strictly additive — valid inputs flow through unchanged. 8 unit tests pin: data.name None / empty rejected, book_format None / empty / non-string rejected, data=None rejected, valid inputs pass through, source-pin AST check that the guard precedes any string concatenation. | #110 | Fork issue [#109](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/109) (reporter: @droM4X) — **regression in v4.0.31**. The app-passwords UI shipped in PR #104 was placed inside the existing profile-save outer `<form>` in `cps/templates/user_edit.html` (which spans lines 176–607). HTML5 forbids nested `<form>` elements; browsers silently ignore the inner `<form>` tag and submit the OUTER form when the inner button is clicked. Result: user clicks "Create app password", browser POSTs to `/me` (profile-save endpoint, not `/me/app-passwords`), label text gets ignored, page reloads with no flash + no token — exactly @droM4X's symptom. Fix moves the entire app-passwords block outside the outer profile `<form>`. 4 unit tests pin the invariant: `<form>` depth-tracker walk over the template asserts no nested forms, plus a stronger pin that asserts the app-password create `<form>` opens at outer-form-nesting-depth 0 specifically. | `08a516fb` | v4.0.35 |
| #111 | Fork issue [#108](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/108) (reporter: @droM4X). `cps.db.CalibreDB.order_authors` was logging `ERROR Author '<name>' not found to display name in right order` on every page render where `Books.author_sort` had drifted from `Authors.sort`. Three changes: (1) module-level `_AUTHOR_SORT_DRIFT_WARNED` set rate-limits to one log line per process per drifted sort string; (2) demote ERROR → WARNING (the function recovers gracefully via the Authors.id fallback loop); (3) replace `break` with `continue` so a single drifted author no longer short-circuits the whole book's author ordering into id-order — only the drifted one falls through. 6 unit tests pin: AST walk asserts `continue` not `break` in `order_authors`, source-pin on the dedup set + WARNING level, behavioral test runs `order_authors` 10× over 3 drifted authors and asserts the dedup set has exactly 3 entries (proving rate-limit), behavioral test on a 2-author book pins that the valid author still gets correctly sort-ordered when one author drifts. | `69c87789` | v4.0.36 |
| #122 | Closes upstream CWA [#243](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/243) (11 reactions, 15 comments — long-standing user request). Opt-in support for user-installed Calibre plugins during ingest, format conversion, cover enforcement, and metadata embed. New env var `CWA_CALIBRE_USER_PLUGINS` (default: off). When the operator sets it to a truthy value, every Calibre subprocess invocation runs with `HOME=/config` so the embedded Calibre process loads any plugin .zip files placed under `/config/.config/calibre/plugins/`; the directory is auto-created at container startup with the right ownership (skipped on `NETWORK_SHARE_MODE=true`). When unset (the default), HOME is inherited from the parent and no third-party Python loads — preserves the existing trust model for deployments that don't ask for it. New helper module `cps/services/calibre_user_plugins.py` (~80 LOC, single-concern, no Flask dependencies) exposes `is_enabled`, `apply_to_env(env)`, `ensure_plugins_dir`, `env_var_name`, `home_path`. | #123 | Follow-up to #122 — found via local Docker e2e test that v4.0.40 was incomplete: just dropping `.zip` files in `/config/.config/calibre/plugins/` didn't make Calibre load them at conversion time. Calibre maintains a registry at `customize.py.json` populated by `calibre-customize -a <zip>`. Without that step, the .zips are inert. This was the user-visible failure mode reported all over upstream CWA #243 ("I copied the plugin folder, nothing happens"). v4.0.41 fixes it: bootstrap now scans the plugins dir for `.zip` files and runs `calibre-customize -a` per file with HOME=/config on first boot, then short-circuits on subsequent boots when the registry is non-empty. New helper function `auto_register_plugins(calibre_customize_binary=...)` returns the list of newly-registered plugin display names. Permission errors / missing binary / nonzero exit codes log + return cleanly so container start is never gated on registration. 9 new regression tests cover: disabled returns empty, missing dir returns empty, populated registry short-circuits, first boot calls binary once per .zip in sorted order, failed subprocess doesn't raise, missing binary doesn't raise, registry parser handles missing/corrupt JSON. Verified end-to-end on local Docker with the canonical plugin set (DeDRM_plugin.zip + Obok_plugin.zip + DeACSM_plugin.zip): all three auto-register on fresh container, persist to customize.py.json, second boot skips re-registration, non-DRM books continue to ingest cleanly with the plugin chain active. Full DRM round-trip not exercised here because the plugins read decryption keys (Kindle serial / ADE / Kobo device key) from `dedrm.json` next to the .zips — those are operator-private and out of scope for autopilot test coverage. | `b0aed3ec` | v4.0.41 |
| TBD | Two production-only bugs caught by deploying #123 to teenyverse and copying real plugin .zips through the bootstrap. **Bug 1 — source-equals-destination collision:** when an operator's source filename matches the plugin's display name (e.g. `DeACSM.zip` → calibre target `<plugins_dir>/DeACSM.zip`), calibre-customize's internal `shutil.copy(source, target)` collapses on the same path and the registration silently fails (source file gets truncated/removed, `customize.py.json` stays unchanged). Fix: stage every source through `tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".zip")` so the destination path can never equal the source path. Side benefit: keeps the operator's original .zip exactly as they dropped it. **Bug 2 — chown gated on NETWORK_SHARE_MODE for the local config volume:** the post-registration chown to `abc:abc` was wrapped in `if not nsm:`, but `/config/.config/calibre` is always a local Docker volume — `NETWORK_SHARE_MODE` is for `/calibre-library` and `/cwa-book-ingest` (NAS-mounted paths). With NSM=true on teenyverse, calibre-extracted plugin contents stayed owned by root after the bootstrap, and the abc service user couldn't read them at conversion time. Fix: chown unconditionally on `/config/.config/calibre`, leave NSM gating only for the NAS-mounted library/ingest dirs. 2 new regression tests pin: tmp-staged path is under the system tmp dir (never under plugins_dir), and the staged tmp file is cleaned up after registration (no per-reboot leak into /tmp). All 43 unit tests green. Verified end-to-end on local Docker: collision filename `DeACSM.zip` registers cleanly, all 3 plugins land in customize.py.json, all files end up `abc:abc`-owned. | `fcb0822a` | v4.0.42 |
| #120 | Cover-picker Kobo preview throughput overhaul. Three issues observed live on `/book/<id>/cover` after v4.0.38 shipped: (1) `threading.BoundedSemaphore(4)` was already wrong from PR #92 onward — the WSGI server is gevent and we don't `monkey.patch_all`, so a synchronous semaphore acquire blocks the entire gevent loop; with 18 candidate covers, login + `/static/` + metadata-search all stall while each Wand job runs serially. PR #119 swapped to `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` which had the same problem because `Future.result()` is a synchronous threading.Event wait that doesn't yield to the gevent hub — confirmed live with `py-spy`: MainThread stuck in `concurrent.futures._base.wait` while a worker did the C call. (2) `_fetch_url_bytes` for external candidate covers (Amazon, OpenLibrary, Google Books, etc.) was running on the gevent main thread inside the picker handler, so a slow upstream stalled every other in-flight request. (3) Each settings change re-fetched all ~18 candidate URLs from scratch, so toggling Edge blur → Gradient took as long as the initial toggle-on. Fixes: switch the pool to `gevent.threadpool.ThreadPool` (yields cleanly via `pool.apply` so the gevent loop stays responsive); fall back to the stdlib executor when gevent isn't importable so unit-test runners stay green. Run the entire fetch-then-pad pipeline on the pool — the gevent main thread never blocks on SSL handshakes. Add a 64 MB LRU URL-bytes cache so subsequent settings changes hit cache for the URL fetch and pay only the Wand cost. Drop the candidate fetch timeout from `(10, 30)` to `(5, 8)` since the picker is interactive (a slow upstream blocks the user's grid; better to drop fast and let them retry). Optimize `edge_blur` itself: blur at quarter resolution and upscale (the upscale acts as its own low-pass filter), 3× faster wall-clock with no perceptible visual difference (0.54 s → 0.24 s on a real cover). Lift the client-side `KOBO_MAX_CONCURRENT` cap from 4 to 8 to match the new server pool. Mark the helper reentrant via `threading.local` so the picker handler can dispatch the whole pipeline to the pool while `render_kobo_preview_data_url` (which also dispatches when called directly) doesn't double-allocate a slot. Live-verified: 18 covers re-render in **~1 second** (down from "never completes in 20 s"); subsequent settings changes (edge_blur → gradient) hit the URL cache and complete in 1 s. **Why the previous releases looked correct in unit tests but wedged in production**: every unit test imports the module without gevent, so the gevent codepath was never exercised; the threading.Semaphore + concurrent.futures regressions were invisible to the test harness. New behavioral check pins the gevent path. 33 unit tests. | `e83d5791` | v4.0.39 |
| #119 | Cover-picker Kobo preview reliability + new `gradient` fill mode. Two issues observed live on `/book/<id>/cover`: (1) changing the **Target aspect ratio** or **Border fill style** dropdowns while "Show how each cover would look on a Kobo" was on did not refresh the previews — the closure-shared `inFlightCount`/`currentBurst` got corrupted when an aborted older burst's `.finally` decremented the counter belonging to the freshly-started new burst, so subsequent fetches looked "in flight" and visible img.src never updated; (2) toggling on with ~36 candidate cards fired 36 simultaneous fetches, each holding a gunicorn worker through the server-side `BoundedSemaphore(4)`, starving login / static / metadata-search routes until the burst drained. Fix replaces the closure-state with a generation counter — every refresh increments `generation`, each fetch closes over `myGen`, and completion handlers only mutate live UI state when `generation === myGen`. Adds a client-side `KOBO_MAX_CONCURRENT = 4` work-queue so the toggle-on burst never exceeds the server's per-process Wand cap. Discrete-event controls (aspect / fill-mode dropdowns) refresh immediately; the manual-color text input keeps the 250 ms debounce. New **`gradient`** fill mode added alongside `edge_mirror` / `edge_blur` / `dominant` / `average` / `manual`: samples the dominant color from the cover's top 10% band and bottom 10% band and renders the pad area as a smooth top→bottom gradient between them via Wand's `pseudo='gradient:'`. Looks "designed" — palette-matched without the edge-replication seams of mirror/blur. New option exposed in both the picker and the admin Settings dropdown. 33 unit tests (4 new JS surface tests for refresh wiring + generation safety + concurrency cap, 2 new Wand round-trip tests for gradient mode, 1 new template-surface test). | `27580c0b` | v4.0.38 |

| #188 | (fork issues [#184](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/184), [#185](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/185)) | **OPDS responses intermittently dropped relationship fields (summary, author, language, tags) for a subset of books per request.** Identical sequential requests against a static library returned different counts — `<summary>` / `<author>` / `<dcterms:language>` / `<category>` would render fully for most books in the feed and empty for one or two, with the affected book varying request-to-request. Live SQL trace via `engine.echo=True` showed nine subquery post-loads against a parent query whose `FROM` clause had been polluted with `LEFT OUTER JOIN books_series_link ... LEFT OUTER JOIN series` despite the OPDS code path never adding those joins; `lazy='subquery'` reproduces the parent's compiled FROM/WHERE/ORDER/LIMIT as the inner subselect of its post-load, and that compile-state leak across the process-captured `CalibreDB.session` (shared across gevent greenlets, running `fill_indexpage`'s two-parent-queries-per-request shape) caused the inner subselect to miss rows for a subset of parent IDs — those rows then had empty relationship collections on the `Book` instance handed to the template. **Fix**: switch all nine `Books` relationships (`authors`, `tags`, `comments`, `data`, `series`, `ratings`, `languages`, `publishers`, `identifiers`) from `lazy='subquery'` to `lazy='selectin'`. `selectin` emits one extra `WHERE parent_id IN (?, ?, ...)` per relationship, atomic, depending only on the parent primary keys batched as an IN clause — never on the parent query's FROM/WHERE/ORDER/LIMIT or compile state. Still an eager loader, so PR #40's `DetachedInstanceError` case (upstream #1067 / #1130 / #1139) remains covered. **Supersedes [PR #40](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/pull/40)** (`bc9386c`, v4.0.16, backport of upstream PR #1279 by @dbraendle) — that PR chose `lazy='subquery'` because it solved the original `DetachedInstanceError`; `lazy='selectin'` solves the same DetachedInstanceError while avoiding the compile-state coupling that made #184 + #185 surface. Both #184 and #185 share this single fix because they're the same bug — the random-panel branch in `fill_indexpage` produces the two-parent-queries-per-request shape that the OPDS path always exercises, regardless of which OPDS endpoint the client hits. Affects every consumer of `Books`: OPDS feeds (visible in #184, #185), Kobo sync (`cps/kobo.py`), KOReader cwasync (`cps/readingservices.py`), Magic Shelves, web UI grid/list/detail. **Repro before fix** (30 sequential `/opds/new` requests against a static 21-book library, v4.0.58 GHCR image): counts varied — iter=1 `sum=1 auth=4 cat=21`, iter=2 `sum=1 auth=6 cat=31`, iter=8 `sum=0 auth=6 cat=15`, iter=16 `sum=1 auth=4 cat=12`, etc. Different books dropped in different iterations; mostly all-or-nothing across the four subquery-loaded relationships but not strictly so (iter=4 once showed Oz with `auth=0 lang=1 cat=0 sum=1` — language + summary present, author + tags gone — independent per-relationship post-load failures, ruling out a top-level "Books not loaded" hypothesis). **Post-fix evidence** (same library, same image-with-patch): 100 sequential `/opds/new` requests all returned `sum=1 auth=6 cat=31` (constant); 50 parallel via `xargs -P 16` all returned identical relationship counts. Plus regression suite: `tests/integration/test_books_relationship_loading.py` source-pins `Books.__mapper__.attrs[name].lazy == 'selectin'` for each of the nine relationships (fails fast if anyone reverts the loader) and behaviorally runs 100 sequential + 50 parallel queries asserting populated collections match the underlying DB row counts. Full SQL trace, compile-state-leakage analysis, and why we did not adopt the symptom-level alternatives (per-request session, per-query `joinedload(...)`, disable random panel) all in [`notes/184-185-DESIGN.md`](notes/184-185-DESIGN.md). **Upstream impact**: CWA's PR #1279 is still OPEN (not merged), so upstream `main` doesn't have this bug — but anyone who applies #1279 will inherit it. Upstream comment queued for that PR. | `e8023170` | v4.0.59 |

| #241 | **H1 safety net — annotation backup with rolling-3 per-book snapshots** (closes fork [#240](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/240)). Passive safeguard behind the upcoming H1 import + view + web-reader-write paths: every INSERT or UPDATE to `kobo_annotation_sync` is captured as a per-`(user_id, book_id)` gzipped JSON snapshot under `/config/annotation-backups/<user_id>/<book_id>/<UTC-iso>.json.gz`, with SHA-256 content-hash dedup so identical state never doubles disk usage and rolling-3 retention so the cap is bounded. Two-phase SQLAlchemy wiring on `Session`: `after_flush` collects `(user_id, book_id)` keys onto a per-session attribute, `after_commit` drains them to a daemon worker so the worker never queries before the source thread's commit lands, `after_rollback` discards pending so a rolled-back tx never produces a phantom backup. New `KoboAnnotationBackup(id, user_id, book_id, created_at, content_hash, file_path, size_bytes, annotation_count)` table for retention queries (`ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 3`). Worker is a single daemon thread + `queue.Queue`; backup work is I/O-bound and never blocks the sync API or any HTTP handler. **Default-on**: any future write path (Hardcover sync today; P3's import endpoint and P5's web-reader create path tomorrow) gets the safety net automatically without each caller having to remember. **19 regression tests** cover model + schema declaration, fresh-install table creation via `add_missing_tables`, single-write produces 1 file + 1 index row, full H1 payload round-trips through gzip+JSON without loss, content-hash dedup short-circuits, mutation produces a new backup, 4 distinct states → exactly 3 files + 3 index rows (oldest unlinked), per-book retention isolation, no-annotation no-op, orphan `book_id IS NULL` skipped at collect-time, two-phase collect / dispatch / rollback wiring, and `enqueue_baseline_for_user` enumerates distinct `book_id` once per book (not once per annotation). **Live `cwn-local` end-to-end**: INSERT triggers `after_flush` + `after_commit` → 357-byte gzip file on disk + index row; UPDATE produces a second; 5 distinct states result in exactly 3 surviving files (rolling-3 enforced); ROLLBACK after mutation clears pending so the queue stays at 0. **Out of scope (follow-up PRs)**: restore endpoint UI, per-user toggle UI (default-on is correct for v1), per-user disk-quota sweeper (rolling-3 is the floor). | `dee31869` | v4.0.81 |

| #260 | (fork issue [#224](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/224) follow-up, reporter @droM4X) | **OPDS 401 on Basic-auth rejection now returns Atom XML** (follow-up to v4.0.92 #255). The v4.0.92 fix registered `@opds.errorhandler(401\|403\|404\|500)` on the OPDS blueprint, which fires for explicit `abort(...)` calls from inside route handlers. But the 401 from missing/wrong Basic-auth credentials goes through `auth.auth_error_callback(401)` directly, which (by default) returns a fully-formed HTML `Response` without raising an `HTTPException` — so the blueprint errorhandler pipeline never fired and OPDS readers still got HTML. | #278 | (CWA issue [#1360](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1360), upstream reporter on Docker Desktop with HDD-backed ingest — reproduced in our code path before fixing) | **Polling watcher no longer hammers HDD-backed ingest folders.** Reporter: "the container keeps touching the folder repeatedly instead of sleeping on real file events. The result is constant drive activity, extra seeks, and sustained read load." Verified in `scripts/watch_fallback.py::scan_once`: unconditionally called `iter_files(root, recursive=True)` every poll interval (default 5s), doing `os.walk(root)` over the entire tree + `os.stat()` on every file. On a 3000-book HDD library that's thousands of disk seeks every 5s. **Fix**: new `_dir_mtime_signature(root, recursive)` produces a cheap `(mtime_ns_hash, size)` tuple of root + immediate subdir mtimes; `scan_once` short-circuits the full walk when prior sig matches current AND index is populated. Linux + macOS bump dir mtime on add/remove — exactly the events ingest cares about. The stabilize-emit path still runs from the gated branch so files mid-flight at gate-close time aren't lost. **7 RED→GREEN tests** in `tests/unit/test_watch_fallback_mtime_gate_1360.py` — headline test patches `iter_files` + asserts `call_count == 0` on a no-change poll, pins the HDD-saving behavior. **Live exercise on cwn-local**: empty-dir → no-change-skip → file-drop reopens gate → `CLOSE_WRITE` emits after stabilize. Zero behavior change under inotify mode (fallback only runs on `CWA_WATCH_MODE=poll` or inotify ENOSPC). | `8b03cc79` | v4.0.109 |
| #277 | (CWA issue [#1364](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1364), today's upstream report — reproduced on our build before fixing per the new "verify upstream issues against our divergent code" discipline) | **Web EPUB reader now persists user position + records read history.** Reporter on the upstream tracker: "opens at the correct cached position then immediately snaps back to the beginning ... book_read_link fields are never updated." | #274 | (CW issue [#3437](https://github.com/janeczku/calibre-web/issues/3437), reporter @rschiefer — 283-day-old upstream report, highest-reach un-drained CW issue at 8 reach) | **Book upload onto a restricted filesystem (CIFS without explicit `file_mode`/`dir_mode`, LinuxServer-style PUID/PGID bind mounts, NFS squash-root shares) no longer surfaces `[Errno 1] Operation not permitted` as a user-visible error even though the bytes already landed at the destination.** Root cause: `cps/helper.py::move_files_on_change`'s cross-device fallback used `shutil.copy2 + os.remove`. `shutil.copy2` is `copyfile` followed by `copystat`; on filesystems that disallow `chmod` for the running uid, `copystat` raises `PermissionError(EPERM)` AFTER `copyfile` has already written the destination. Pre-fix code re-raised the EPERM, masking the data-side success. **Fix**: new `cps/services/file_move.py::copy_with_metadata_fallback` helper tries `shutil.copy2` first (preserves mode + atime/mtime + xattr); on `OSError`, retries with `shutil.copyfile` (data only). Destination gets default umask permissions — acceptable for the upload path because the file is about to be re-processed by the Calibre ingest pipeline. Three call sites in `cps/helper.py` route through the helper: `rename_all_files_on_change` + 2 in `move_files_on_change` (upload path + multi-file merge loop). **13 RED→GREEN tests** in `tests/unit/test_file_move_metadata_fallback.py` (10) + `tests/unit/test_move_files_chmod_eperm.py` (3) — helper happy path, EPERM fallback, EACCES same, ENOSPC propagates, real-data round-trip, source-pins for the 3 call sites + import + no remaining direct `shutil.copy2`; integration through `move_files_on_change` (EPERM tolerated, `localbook.path` updated on success, genuine copy failure surfaces). 189/190 helper-adjacent tests pass. Credit @rschiefer for the original report. | `eab384c0` | v4.0.106 |

| #271 | (CWA issue [#1339](https://github.com/crocodilestick/Calibre-Web-Automated/issues/1339), reporter @Altycoder, +1 @ragaskar) | **Home grid no longer shows wrong covers after a library wipe + re-ingest.** `ub.Thumbnail` rows are keyed by `entity_id = book.id` (no UUID, no content hash). When a library is wiped and a different one is ingested, old Thumbnail records + their on-disk files survive and serve for the re-used `book.id` values — `get_book_cover_internal` only checked "is the file present on disk?", never compared `book.last_modified` vs `thumbnail.generated_at`. The book detail page used the `og` resolution (no Thumbnail rows → falls through to on-disk `cover.jpg` → correct cover) while the home grid used `sm/md/lg` via `get_cover_srcset` → hit the stale rows → wrong cover. **Fix**: in `get_book_cover_internal`, treat thumbnails whose `generated_at` predates the book's `last_modified` as missing. The existing background-regenerate branch fires AND the request falls through to on-disk `cover.jpg` — user sees the right cover immediately, a fresh thumbnail is written for subsequent loads. Inline `_stale` helper is defensive: returns False on missing data, normalizes tz-aware/tz-naive datetime mismatch. **6 RED→GREEN tests** in `tests/unit/test_cover_thumbnail_staleness_1339.py` source-pin the comparison + exercise the helper via `exec`. **Live container repro on cwn-local**: swapped book_2's thumbnail file with book_3's content + aged `generated_at` to 2025-01-01 → pre-fix `/cover/2/sm` → `image/webp` md5=`dd3b2c84` (wrong book) → post-fix call 1 → `image/jpeg` md5=`a019ed9d` (matches on-disk Dorian Gray cover) → call 2 after 5s background regen → `image/webp` md5=`8699aec7` (regenerated correctly). 264 cover/thumbnail-adjacent tests pass in isolation. Also addresses @Altycoder's gripe that "Scheduled Thumbnail Refresh" doesn't fix it — even if the scheduled task is killed mid-batch, the read path now self-heals stale records as users browse. | `42478883` | v4.0.103 |
| #270 | (fork issue [#256](https://github.com/new-usemame/Calibre-Web-NextGen/issues/256) verification feedback, reporter @droM4X) | **Bottom paginator chevrons now vertically align with the numbered buttons + ≥20px bottom margin.** After v4.0.94 shipped, @droM4X noted in his verification reply that the chevron prev/next items rendered visually above the boxed numerals (default `vertical-align: baseline` on inline-block items aligns text baselines — shorter-content chevrons float to the top of the row) and the bottom margin was too tight. **Fix**: `vertical-align: middle` on every `.page-item` inside `.pagination.pagination-bottom`, plus explicit `margin-bottom: 24px` (caliBlur's root font-size is ~10px so `1.5rem` resolves to only 15px — the rem unit would silently fall below droM4X's 20px request). **2 new regression tests** pin both invariants. **Playwright pilot on cwn-local** with `config_books_per_page=4`: all 6 page-items (prev chevron, 4 numbered buttons, next chevron) share `center=y616` to the pixel; computed `margin-bottom: 24px`; top paginator unchanged (`position: fixed; top: 58.1px; right: 0`). | `591e4658` | v4.0.102 |

| #230 | (operator-flagged 2026-05-17 borrow-day session; A2 in `notes/KOBO-A1-A2-B8-PROMPT.md`) | **Admin per-book "Resend to Kobo" action** on admin → Edit User, alongside the existing *Force Full Kobo Sync* button. Admin enters a book ID, clicks **Resend**, and on the user's next sync the device receives that one book as `NewEntitlement` (forcing a fresh download). Avoids the nuclear "re-sync everything" path when a single book gets corrupted on device, has a stale cover, or needs to pick up a post-sync format conversion. **Mechanism, twofold:** (1) delete `(user_id, book_id)` from `kobo_synced_books` so the next sync emits `NewEntitlement` rather than `ChangedEntitlement`; (2) bump `Books.last_modified = datetime.now(timezone.utc)` so the sync filter `Books.last_modified > sync_token.books_last_modified` picks the book up regardless of where the device's cursor sits. Either step alone is a partial fix — deletion alone leaves a book stuck behind an advanced cursor; the timestamp bump alone produces a `ChangedEntitlement`, not a re-delivery. **Endpoint** `POST /ajax/kobo_resend/<int:userid>/<int:bookid>` — `@user_login_required` + `@admin_required`, integer-coerced at the routing layer (`<int:...>` rejects non-numeric paths at routing), CSRF-protected via the global `ajaxSetup` `beforeSend` hook. **UI** block on `user_edit.html` under the existing Kobo Sync Token section: book-ID number input + Resend button + inline feedback span; hidden behind `{% if current_user.role_admin() %}` so non-admin viewers never see it; show/hide in lockstep with the Force Full Kobo Sync button (token-deletion / token-creation modal hooks updated). | #340 | **A new cover now shows up everywhere immediately — web UI and Kobo.** Applying a cover via the focused cover-picker (`POST /book/<id>/cover/apply`) saved `has_cover` and busted the picker's own `?ts=` preview but never bumped `book.last_modified`. The post-commit best-effort steps were split from the critical DB write so a commit failure now returns 500 instead of a false `ok:True`. **Discoverability**: the cover image itself is now the entry to the picker on the book detail page — an always-visible corner camera badge (discoverable on touch) plus a hover/focus "Change cover" overlay; the edit-page button was relabeled from "Open focused cover picker" to "Change cover" (no overlay on the edit page, to avoid discarding unsaved form edits on an accidental click).
